MEMORANDUM OF UNDERSTANDING
AMONG
CITY OF BRISBANE, CITY OF BURLINGAME, CITY OF DALY CITY, CITY OF 
MILLBRAE, CITY OF PACIFICA, CITY OF SAN BRUNO, CITY OF SAN MATEO, 
AND
THE HOUSING ENDOWMENT AND REGIONAL TRUST
 OF SAN MATEO COUNTY
FOR THE
MULTI-JURISDICTIONAL DISPARATE IMPACT ANALYSIS
This Memorandum of Understanding (“MOU”), effective the ____ day of ______ 2025, is entered 
into by and among the City of Brisbane, the City of Burlingame, the City of Daly City, the City of 
Millbrae, the City of Pacifica, the City of San Bruno, the City of San Mateo (“PARTICIPATING 
JURISDICTION”), and the Housing Endowment and Regional Trust of San Mateo County (HEART), 
together referred to herein as the "PARTIES."
RECITALS
WHEREAS, the County of San Mateo and the cities and towns in San Mateo County have a strong 
history of collaboration and resource sharing on various planning studies and initiatives as part of 
the 21 Elements Planning Collaborative, which among other jurisdictions includes the 
PARTICIPATING JURISDICTION; and
WHEREAS, one such outgrowth of this collaboration was the establishment of the Housing Consulting 
Services Program at HEART, of which City of Brisbane, the City of Burlingame, the City of Millbrae, the 
City of Pacifica, and the City of San Bruno, among other jurisdictions have contracted for services; and 
WHEREAS, HEART initiated the Multi-Jurisdictional Disparate Impact Analysis (the “PROJECT”); and 
the purpose of this PROJECT is to complete a Disparate Impact Analysis that complies with the legal 
and regulatory requirements for establishing local preference policies for affordable housing for each 
PARTICIPATING JURISDICTION; and
WHEREAS, the PARTICIPATING JURISDICTION can complete the PROJECT at a reduced cost by 
sharing analysis and resources for greater efficiency; and
WHEREAS, through competitive bidding and a request for proposal (“RFP”) process facilitated by 
HEART, Street Level Advisors (“CONTRACTOR”) was chosen as the firm to provide consulting 
services associated with the PROJECT; and
WHEREAS, HEART has served as the project manager (“PROJECT MANAGER”) for this collaborative 
effort through initial formation and the RFP process to ensure that the voice of each 
PARTICIPATING JURISDICTION is heard and their needs are addressed; and
136 of 349

--- page 137 ---
Page 2 of 15
WHEREAS, HEART will continue to serve as the PROJECT MANAGER for the collaborative effort for 
the duration of the PROJECT; and
WHEREAS, HEART will also serve as fiscal agent for the PROJECT and will enter into a contract with 
CONTRACTOR and oversee the payment of invoices the PROJECT work; and 
WHEREAS,  the PARTICIPATING JURISDICTIONS enter into this Memorandum of Understanding with 
the HEART outlining the roles of each PARTICIPATING JURISDICTION, the CONTRACTOR, HEART, and 
the funding obligations for the PROJECT.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED that the PARTIES agree as follows:

JURISDICTIONS agree to use the CONTRACTOR and PROJECT MANAGER as the consulting team, (3) 
HEART is serving as a FISCAL AGENT to facilitate the PROJECT,

Exhibit B – Project Management Scope from HEART
Exhibit C – Project Budget and Agency Costs

funding as set forth in Exhibit C for the PROJECT and perform the obligations outlined in the 
Work Program set forth in Exhibit A, including participation in the overall study development. 
B.
PROJECT MANAGER AND FISCAL AGENT: HEART, a Joint Powers Authority and non-profit 
corporation noncorporation, shall serve as PROJECT MANAGER and FISCAL AGENT and shall 
manage and implement all aspects of the PROJECT, in accordance with the Project 
Management Scope set forth in Exhibit B. HEART shall enter into a separate contract with 
CONTRACTOR and shall review and pay all invoices due to the CONTRACTOR. 
C.
CONTRACTOR: Street Level Advisors, a California corporation, shall serve as the consultant

PARTIES.

process set forth in Section VI. All PARTIES agree to use best efforts in such case to reach 
agreement without causing a PROJECT delay. At the time the project budget reaches 80% of

the PARTIES.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  6
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 10-4662
File ID: 25-10583
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
December 01, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Marina Lagoon Pump Station Physical Hydraulic Model Study — Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Northwest Hydraulic Consultants, Ltd. to provide professional design services for the Marina 
Lagoon Pump Station Physical Hydraulic Model Study project in the amount of $233,010; establish a contingency reserve in 
the amount of $34,900; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form 
presented, and execute any future amendments within the contingency amount, including no-cost term extension 
amendments.
BACKGROUND:
Marina Lagoon, originally known as Seal Slough, is an approximately four-mile-long water body that meanders through the 
City and functions as both a flood control and recreational facility. Flows within the lagoon are regulated by tide gates 
along the southern end and by the Marina Lagoon Pump Station at the northern end. Constructed in the mid-1980s, the 
station consists of five pumps used to regulate lagoon levels between elevations 97.0 feet and 95.0 feet, with the ability to 
draw the lagoon down to elevation 93.4 feet for maintenance.
Pump/engine system failures that occurred during the New Year’s Eve 2022 storm event prompted staff to evaluate the 
operations of the Marina Lagoon Pump Station. According to the pump manufacturer, the pumps at Marina Lagoon are 
not recommended to operate below elevation 95.0 feet. Pumping below this level can result in avoidable wear and 
operational issues with the equipment. Historically, staff pumped the Marina Lagoon to levels below 95.0 feet to provide 
an annual period during which residents with docks could perform maintenance while the water level was low; staff has 
ceased this practice upon learning the pump manufacturer’s recommendations.
In order to preserve the long-term flood control capability and to continue providing a maintenance period for dock 
residents, staff are seeking qualified engineering firms to evaluate the performance of the existing pumps to assess their 
efficiency and identify potential improvements to system operations. Given the size of the Marina Lagoon pumps, a 
physical hydraulic model is necessary to assess intake flow patterns and identify potential improvements to optimize pump 
efficiency and performance and determine if pumping below 95.0 feet is advisable.
On July 3, 2025, the City issued a Request for Proposals (RFP) for professional design services to perform the physical 
hydraulic model study. Two proposals were received by the due date of July 31, 2025. After scoring the proposals and 
subsequently conducting interviews, City staff determined that Northwest Hydraulic Consultants, Ltd. was the most 
qualified firm due to their technical expertise and relevant experience. Therefore, staff recommends awarding a 
professional design services agreement to Northwest Hydraulic Consultants, Ltd. 
156 of 349

--- page 157 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Consultant shall perform the following tasks:
•
Task 1 – Model Design and Workplan
The Consultant shall prepare and submit a draft and final modeling workplan to the City for 
review and approval. The workplan shall include a description of the existing pump system and 
the pump station’s hydraulic parameters, the study objectives, a description of similitude 
criteria at the selected scale, potential scaling effects, testing methodology, test program 
(including the proposed number of tests and model modifications), documentation and 
instrumentation, and drawings detailing the model layout.
The model scale shall be selected to meet the scaling requirements as outlined in ANSI/HI 9.8-
2024. The physical model shall be designed and operated in adherence to the Froude criterion 
for dynamic similarity. It is anticipated that the model shall be constructed at an undistorted 
length scale of approximately 1:12, which shall be confirmed during workplan development 
upon receipt of all information required for model design. The final scale may be adjusted 
slightly to accommodate commercially available cast acrylic tubing.  
The City shall provide all dimensional drawings and relevant information required for model 
design in PDF format and AutoCAD-compatible format if available.
•
Task 2 – Model Construction
The Consultant shall fabricate the physical model as detailed herein. The Principal-in-Charge 
and Lead Modeling Engineer shall provide technical input during the model construction as 
required and verify that all fabrication tolerances are attained.
The physical model shall reproduce an approximately 180 ft wide section of the Marina Lagoon, 
extending approximately 80 ft upstream of the intake weir and including the riprapped slopes 
adjacent to the wet well entrance. A constant bed elevation in the lagoon of 91.0 shall be 
represented as a fixed bed.
The model shall include the intake weir, headwall, trash screen, and the internal geometry of 
the wet well, including the support columns and pump bay walls, the approximate outer 
diameter of the pumps, and the internal geometry of the section inlets up to the throat of the 
pump bells. Due to scaling limitations, the model trash screen shall be designed to simulate the 
headloss (open area) and flow-turning (aspect ratio) characteristic of the prototype screen 
rather than a direct scale of the individual bars or screen mesh.
The estimated model footprint is approximately 18 feet wide x 15 feet long x 2 feet deep. The 
model shall be constructed using a combination of dimensional lumber, treated and sealed with 
epoxy or other water-resistant coatings, and clear acrylic plastic in key areas around the pump 
bays, allowing for flow visualization. Internal model structures shall be fabricated to allow 
166 of 349

--- page 167 ---
Design Professional Services 2024
Page 8 of 13
Rev 1/24
adjustments as required, and to accommodate potential lowering of pumps. The model shall be 
capable of simulating flows up to the pump station’s capacity of 750,000 GPM. 
•
Task 3 – Model Testing
Testing shall assess the performance of the existing design, evaluate potential design 
modifications if unsatisfactory performance is identified, and document the proposed final 
design configuration.
Testing shall be conducted under steady-state conditions, maintaining a constant water level 
with inflow equal to outflow. The total model inflow, the individual model pump flows, and the 
wet well operating level shall be set in accordance with the testing program. Model 
measurements and instrumentation shall be in accordance with ANSI/HI 9.8-2024. Pre-swirl 
instrumentation shall be installed at each pump, and velocity instrumentation shall be installed 
at the pump expected to experience the most adverse flow conditions. The pump columns shall 
be designed for interchangeability to permit relocation of velocity instrumentation, if required.
A test program shall be developed as part of the modeling workplan in collaboration with the 
City and will include a range of operating scenarios (combinations of water levels, flow rates, 
and pumps in service). The test scenarios shall be based on information from the City on 
anticipated operating conditions, experience, and engineering judgement.
Task 3.1 – Existing Design Testing
The performance of the existing design shall be evaluated at up to four (4) operating scenarios. 
The existing design (testing program shall include tests to investigate the hydraulic performance 
for both four and five active pump operations down to a water level of El. 95.0 ft, and single-
pump operation at a water level of El. 93.0 ft.
Task 3.2 – Design Development Testing
Design development testing shall be conducted to evaluate possible geometry changes or 
additions to the existing configuration if unsatisfactory pump performance is identified. Design 
modifications shall be developed collaboratively with the City and are expected to be restricted 
to adding/modifying devices within the wet well (e.g., fillets, flow splitters, vanes, flow 
conditioners, baffles, etc.). Design development testing shall be conducted for the operating 
scenario(s) identified during existing design testing as providing the most adverse flow 
conditions to the pumps.
Task 3.3 – Witness Testing
A formal one-day witness test shall be conducted at the Consultant’s laboratory toward the end 
of design development testing. The witness test shall include an introductory presentation 
describing the model domain boundaries, scaling and similitude, model instrumentation and 
documentation, model testing program, and a summary of the test results collected to-date. 
The presentation shall be followed by a hands-on demonstration of the model for various 
operating conditions, demonstrating both the existing conditions and the recommended design 
configuration. If requested by the City, the witness test shall include live video and audio for 
remote participants.
167 of 349

--- page 168 ---
Design Professional Services 2024
Page 9 of 13
Rev 1/24
Task 3.4 – Evaluate Lowered Pumps
The Consultant shall evaluate and adjust the vertical discharge column of the model pumps to 
lower the suction bell elevation and reduce the floor-to-bell clearance. The lowered pump 
configuration shall be evaluated for up to four (4) model tests. 
Task 3.5 – Final Design Detailed Documentation Testing
Consultant shall document the performance of the final design over a range of operating 
conditions. Consultant shall perform a maximum of eight (8) operating scenarios which shall be 
evaluated as part of final design detailed documentation testing.
•
Task 4 – Reporting
Following completion of model testing, the Consultant shall prepare a technical report (draft 
and final) summarizing the results of the physical model study, including details (description 
and drawings) of all modifications required to correct identified hydraulic anomalies or other 
unsatisfactory flow conditions. The report shall contain a description of the model, scaling 
criteria, test procedures, relevant photographs, and a complete description of the test results, 
including observations and tabular data. 
Photographs and unedited video footage recorded during testing shall be uploaded to the 
project SharePoint site for City access.
The draft report shall be submitted in electronic (PDF) format within two weeks of completing 
model testing. The City shall provide a consolidated set of review comments within 
approximately one week of receipt. The Consultant shall submit the final report in electronic 
(PDF) format within one week of receiving the City’s comments.
•
Task 5 – Model Decommissioning
Approximately one week following the submission of the final report, the physical model shall 
be dismantled and disposed of.
•
Task 6 – Project Management
The Consultant shall develop the project schedule, manage work progression, prepare monthly 
invoices, monitor task budgets, prepare monthly progress reports, and implement a quality 
control plan.
The Consultant shall host a project kick-off meeting and up to four (4) additional meetings to 
present progress updates and interim results at key milestones. These meetings will be held 
virtually, unless otherwise requested by the City, using Microsoft Teams and be limited to a 1-
hour duration each. The Consultant shall prepare the meeting agenda, presentation, and 
minutes for the meeting. 
At the onset of the Project, the Consultant shall set up a SharePoint site for sharing project 
deliverables including the work plan submittal, the model layout drawings submittal, meeting 
agendas and minutes, key correspondence that is evidence of the transmittal of key project 
168 of 349

deliverables; the draft and final report submittals and select photos and unedited video 
footage.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if CONSULTANT 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall 
be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. If a Notice 
of Cancellation endorsement is not available, CONSULTANT shall ensure the requisite Notice of 
173 of 349

--- page 174 ---
Design Professional Services 2024
Page 13 of 13
Rev 1/24
Cancellation is specified in the Certificate of Insurance.  In the event the Notice of Cancellation is not 
specified in the Certificate of Insurance, Consultant shall be responsible for providing the City the 
requisite notice as specified in this Exhibit C. 
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
December 01, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Bay Meadows MU3, Final Map & Subdivision Improvement — Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve the Bay Meadows MU3 final map and accept the dedication for a public access easement as 
shown on the final map; approve the subdivision improvement agreement with Bay Meadows MU3 Office Investors, LLC 
and Bay Meadows MU3 Residential Investors, LLC; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in 
substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The Planning Commission approved the application for a modification to a Site Plan and Architectural Review for Bay 
Meadows MU3 (PA-2020-053) on June 11, 2021. The project consists of a 4-story commercial building with approximately 
121,000 square-feet of office space and 5,600 square-feet of ground floor active space along South Delaware Street and a 
4-story residential building with 67 dwelling units along West Kyne Street on a 1.5-acre site. Since the project proposes 12 
commercial condominiums and 67 residential condominiums and merges the two existing lots, a final map was required as 
a Condition of Approval. The project was also required to dedicate a pedestrian passage easement as a Condition of 
Approval to accommodate a public access path through the project site. 
In July 2025, the developer filed a final map application with the City in compliance with the Conditions of Approval, 
Subdivision Map Act, and San Mateo Municipal Code Title 26. The final map includes a dedication for a pedestrian passage 
easement for public access. The final map was reviewed for accuracy and completeness by the City’s survey and mapping 
consultant, CSG Consultants. A copy of the final map is included as Attachment 2. 
The developer is requesting the final map be approved and recorded prior to the completion of the project’s right-of-way 
improvements which includes replacing an existing driveway with standard sidewalk, landscaping strip, and curb and 
restoring other portions of the sidewalk affected by service lateral installations. Government Code Section 66462(a) 
requires the developer to enter into a subdivision improvement agreement with the City to ensure completion of the 
work. The associated improvement plans were prepared by the developer’s engineer and are compliant with the City 
standards, and to the satisfaction of the Public Works Director. The subdivision improvement agreement is included as 
Attachment 3. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Approval of the final map and subdivision improvement agreement will have no budgetary impact. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

R E C I T A L S  
A. 
Subdivider is the owner of that certain tract of land, more particularly described in  Exhibit A 
attached hereto and incorporated herein by this reference, located at 2955 S. Delaware Street      
in the City of San Mateo, County of San Mateo, State of California. 
B. 
Subdivider’s application for a vesting tentative map was approved by the San Mateo Planning 
Commission on June 22, 2021, subject to various conditions. 
C.

("Map"), incorporated herein by reference. 
D. 
Subdivider has requested approval of the Map prior to the completion of improvements. 
E. 
The Map designates pedestrian access easements for the City, and Subdivider proposes to 
dedicate such easements to the City.  
F.

various off-site sidewalk improvements and off-site landscape improvements.   
G. 
Subdivider has already provided funds in the form of a Security Deposit in the amount of 
$52,892.51 for the completion of certain improvements required under Subdivider’s Conditions 
of Approval 
H. 
City desires to assure that the improvements will be done in a good and workmanlike manner, 
in accordance with the Conditions of Approval for the Vesting Tentative Tract Map approved by 
the City on June 22, 2021, per City, state and federal standards.

satisfactory performance by Subdivider of Subdivider's obligations under the tentative map conditions 
of approval, the Subdivision Map Act, and the San Mateo Municipal Code, the parties agree as follows:

C.  
City shall have the right, without limitation of other rights or remedies, to draw upon or 
utilize any improvement security furnished hereunder to mitigate the City’s damages in the 
event of Subdivider's default. 
1. The City may serve written notice of any default upon the surety on any corporate 
surety bond furnished as improvement security hereunder, and request that the surety 
take over and complete the Required Improvements. If the surety, within seven (7) days 
after service of such notice of default, does not give the City written notice of its 
intention to perform this Agreement, or does not commence performance within five (5) 
days after notice to the City of its intention to perform, the City may take over the work 
and prosecute the same to completion, by contract or by other method the City deems 
advisable, for the account and at the expense of the Subdivider and its surety. 
2.  Subdivider acknowledges that the estimated total costs and Required Improvement 
security amounts set forth herein may not reflect the actual cost of construction or 
installation of the Required Improvements, and consequently, City's damages for 
Subdivider's default shall be measured by the cost of completing the Required 
Improvements. If the damages incurred by the City in taking over and completing any 
portion of the Required Improvements exceed the principal amount of the Required 
Improvement security, then the Subdivider shall reimburse the City in the amount of 
such excess damages.

information may lead to rejection of document recording.

must not cover text or lines.  If seal impression smudges, re-seal if a sufficient area permits, 
otherwise complete a different acknowledgment form.

Subdivider shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract insurance against claims for injuries to 
persons or damage to property which may arise from or in connection with the performance of the work 
hereunder and the results of that work by the Subdivider, his agents, representatives, employees, or

Asbestos Pollution Liability, coverage should be maintained for a minimum of five (5) years after contract 
completion. 
MINIMUM SCOPE AND LIMIT OF INSURANCE  
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office Form CG 00 01 covering CGL on an “occurrence” 
basis, including products and completed operations, property damage, bodily injury and personal & 
advertising injury with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit applies, 
either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location (ISO CG 25 03 or 25 04) or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.   
2. Automobile Liability:  Insurance Services Office Form Number CA 0001 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
Contractor has no owned autos, hired (Code 8) and non-owned (Code 9) autos, with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation insurance as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury or disease.  
4. Contractors Pollution Liability and/or Asbestos Pollution Liability and/or Errors & Omissions applicable to 
the work being performed, with a limit no less than $2,000,000 per claim or occurrence and $2,000,000 
aggregate per policy period of one year. 
5. 
If the Subdivider maintains broader coverage and/or higher limits than the minimums shown above, the 
City requires and shall be entitled to the broader coverage and/or higher limits maintained by the Subdivider. Any 
available insurance proceeds in excess of the specified minimum limits of insurance and coverage shall be available 
to the City.

retroactive date prior to the contract effective date, the Subdivider must purchase an extended period 
coverage for a minimum of five (5) years after completion of contract work.

Liability shall not contain lead-based paint or asbestos exclusions. If the services involve mold identification

“Pollution” shall include microbial matter including mold.

SUBJECT:
28th Avenue Hillsdale Gap Closure — Amendment  
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 2 to the funding agreement with the San Mateo County Transportation Authority for the 
Hillsdale Caltrain Station Bicycle Access Gap Closure Project to extend the term through December 31, 2026, and authorize 
the City Manager to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
In September 2020, the City submitted an application to the San Mateo County Transportation Authority (SMCTA) for the 
Measure A/W Pedestrian and Bicycle Program Cycle 5 Call for Projects. The application proposed improvements to the El 
Camino Real and 28th Avenue crossing for pedestrians and bicyclists through the Hillsdale Caltrain Station Bicycle Access 
Gap Closure project (Project). In December 2020, the City received notification that SMCTA had awarded $153,000 to 
design pedestrian and bicycle improvements between the existing 28th Avenue bicycle boulevard and the new Hillsdale 
Caltrain Station.
In September 2022, an agreement was awarded to Belleci & Associates, Inc. for design services, including community 
engagement. The agreement was amended in June 2023 to expand the project scope to include 28th Avenue from the 
Hillsdale Caltrain Station to East Kyne Street. Since awarding the design contract to Belleci & Associates, the project team 
has held multiple community meetings and advanced the design to 35% completion. Due to staff shortages and vacancies 
in the transportation section, the project is currently on hold.
In March 2024, Amendment No. 1 between SMCTA and the City was executed to extend the Cycle 5 grant to December 30, 
2025. Due to ongoing staff shortages, the City and SMCTA have agreed to Amendment No. 2, which will extend the grant 
at no cost, to December 31, 2026, to complete the Project design.
Staff recommend approving this no cost amendment that will extend the use of the grant funds to December 31, 2026.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact associated with this item.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This item is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

EXHIBIT A-2: SCOPE OF WORK INFORMATION
Hillsdale Caltrain Station Bicycle Access Gap Closure
Sponsoring Agency:
City of San Mateo
Lead/Implementing Agency:
City of San Mateo 
Contact:
Jay Yu 
Engineering Manager
(650) 522-7323
jyu@cityofsanmateo.org 
330 W. 20th Avenue, San Mateo CA 94403 
Project Description and Scope of Work:  
The project scope includes funding for the Plans, Specifications, and Estimates (PS&E) and 
Environmental phases. Design and environmental review for Class IV bikeway from Edison 
Street to El Camino Real, ADA ramp installation, new crosswalk and pedestrian push buttons, 
and signalization modification at El Camino Real intersection, including design for video 
detection for bicyclists and vehicles. Scope includes coordination and permitting with Caltrans 
for intersection improvements.
Bicycle and pedestrian facilities are proposed for either side of the El Camino Real intersection; 
the lack of linkage across the intersection renders them less attractive for users. With no clear 
direction and facilities, users are left to determine safe crossing options on their own across a 
busy six-lane roadway.
This project will define the connection across El Camino Real, providing a link between the east 
and west sides of the intersection that is safe for bicyclists and pedestrians of all ages and 
abilities. This increases the share of active transportation users who can access transit and key 
amenities on both sides of the intersection. By designing (and later implementing) proposed 
features including a Class IV separated bike lane, pedestrian crosswalk, a new accessible curb 
ramp, and video detection, staff intends to eliminate a stressful gap in the City’s active 
transportation network and provide accessibility for users to feel comfortable walking and 
biking.

SUBJECT:
2024 Rail Corridor Transportation Management Association Annual Report – Acceptance
RECOMMENDATION:
Review and accept the 2024 San Mateo Rail Corridor Transportation Management Association (TMA) Annual Report.
BACKGROUND:
In 2005, the City adopted the San Mateo Rail Corridor Transit Oriented Development Plan (Corridor Plan) with the goal to
“allow, encourage, and provide guidance for the creation of world class transit-oriented development (TOD) within a half-
mile radius of the Hillsdale and Hayward Park Caltrain station areas, while maintaining and improving the quality of life for
those who already live and work in the area.” The Corridor Plan includes a framework for (1) creation of a Transit Oriented
Development (TOD), (2) implementation of a Transportation Demand Management (TDM) program with a goal of
achieving an overall reduction in new vehicle trips by at least 25 percent corridor-wide, (3) establishment of trip
generation thresholds, (4) establishment of parking standards, and (5) monitoring of trip generation.
The Corridor Plan established a new TOD zone, which generally encompasses key parcels located within a half mile of the
Hillsdale and Hayward Park Caltrain stations. This new land use includes transit-supportive development densities, building 
heights, and design guidelines. The broader Corridor Plan area extends beyond the TOD zone and includes other areas in
close proximity to these stations. The Corridor Plan also called for the creation of a San Mateo Rail Corridor Transportation
Management Association (TMA). Participation in the TMA is (1) required for all new development within the TOD zone, (2)
strongly encouraged for all new development within the broader Corridor Plan area, and (3) available to any existing uses
outside of the Corridor Plan area (Policy 7.18 of the Corridor Plan).
The TMA comprises developers and developer representatives that have, or are planning, significant development within
the Corridor Plan area. The City participates as a non-voting Board member and does not pay dues to the TMA. The City
Council has nominated the Director of Public Works as the City representative to the TMA Board of Directors. The City’s
role in the TMA is to provide oversight of each applicable development project’s mandated participation as required in
each project’s Conditions of Approval (COA).
Annual Report Process
The TMA facilitates data collection regarding the number of vehicle trips generated by each development per the
individual project’s approved TDM plan. Trip generation is determined by collecting driveway counts at all occupied
developments. These data are compared to the allowable trip generation threshold identified in each development’s COA.
A development is deemed non-compliant if the observed number of vehicle trips exceeds its trip generation threshold. The 
TMA Board of Directors hired a data collection firm and traffic engineering consultant to collect relevant data and prepare 
the 2024 Annual Report (attached).
202 of 349

--- page 203 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
2024 Annual Report Summary
As of the 2024 Annual Report, 26 individual projects have been completed/constructed. Per the prepared report by the
TMA, most projects were below their short-term trip thresholds on their individual project COAs. One (1) project stood out 
as notable in the 2024 Annual TMA Report.
•
Delaware Pacific-2000 Delaware (Shared Driveway)
Delaware Pacific-2000 Delaware share a common driveway, and their trip generation is calculated collectively. 
During the PM peak period, the recorded trip generation was 67 trips, exceeding the short-term collective goal of 
52 trips by 15. This represents an increase of 10 trips compared to the previous year (2023). According to the 
Corridor Plan Policy 7.24, “Projects that exceed their trip generation threshold shall be required to modify their 
trip reduction and parking management plan and incorporate TDM measures that are expected to increase trip 
reduction.”
Per their original TDM plan, both properties are required to provide subsidized transit passes for one year, offer 
bicycle storage, participate in the TMA, promote alternative transportation options, and designate an on-site 
transportation coordinator to manage vehicle and bicycle parking assignments, as well as monitor compliance. 
Delaware Pacific has exceeded these requirements by implementing some more robust TDM measures, including:
•
Providing transit passes (Way2Go) to all residents for over 10 years.
•
Enrolling all residents in the Clipper BayPass program since 2022.
•
Conducting resident surveys to analyze travel origins and destinations.
•
Installing a transit information screen.
•
Promoting commute.org educational meetings to encourage alternative transportation.
Despite these efforts, the combined trip generation for Delaware Pacific and 2000 Delaware continues to exceed
both short-term and long-term thresholds. Staff have been collaborating with MidPen Housing, which now
manages both properties, to identify additional trip reduction measures. MidPen Housing is committed to
reducing trips and has agreed to:
•
Extend the Way2Go free transit pass program, a subsidized fare program offered by SamTrans providing 
unlimited rides on all local and express bus routes for all 2000 Delaware residents, and
•
Include residents in surveys to better understand travel and transit patterns. 
These measures are expected to reduce vehicle reliance and overall trips.
•
Bay Meadows Phase II
The Bay Meadows Phase II development has three trip thresholds based on the progress of the development and 
the completion of grade-separated crossings at 28th and 31st Avenues. The project is currently evaluated against 
the medium-term threshold. In 2024, the development generated 2,454 PM peak hour trips, which is below the 
medium-term threshold of 2,878 trips. This represents an approximate 12% increase from 2023 but remains under 
the threshold. Currently, only two developments, MU-2 and MU-3, remain unfinished in Bay Meadows Phase II, 
with completion expected in two years.
o

Commission Feedback and Staff Recommendation
The TMA and its consultant presented the 2024 Annual Report to the Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission (SIC) on 
September 10, 2025. The presentation included a survey of member projects, an assessment of TDM measures offered to 
residents and tenants, and supporting data collection and analysis. The Commission reviewed the report and unanimously 
recommended that the City Council accept it. Commissioners provided feedback on trip-threshold compliance monitoring, 
coordination with projects not meeting thresholds, and the collection of additional data on effective TDM measures to 
inform the ongoing Citywide TDM Ordinance. Commissioners were pleased to learn that City staff has been working with 
the Delaware Pacific–2000 Delaware property, which will now offer transit passes to all tenants to achieve compliance 
with its trip caps going above and beyond what is in their entitled TDM plan. 
Staff have reviewed the data analysis and report prepared for the TMA Board of Directors and recommend that the City 
Council accept the 2024 Annual Report.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact associated with this item. The TMA is an IRS 501(c)(4) organization that is funded by its
participating members. No City funds are used to pay for the activities of the TMA.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This item is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

Executive Summary 
This report details the results of vehicle trip monitoring conducted under the San Mateo Rail Corridor 
Transit-Oriented Development Plan (Corridor Plan). It also presents a qualitative overview of Transportation 
Demand Management (TDM) plans for completed projects in the Rail Corridor area and a summary of the 
results of a San Mateo Rail Corridor Transportation Management Association (TMA) members’ survey.  
Construction continued in the Corridor Plan area during the 2024 calendar year, including completion of 
apartments on Residential Block 6 and site work on Mixed-Use Blocks 3A and 3B. Area construction 
activities related to the City’s Clean Water project were completed when trip monitoring data were 
collected. By inspection, development in the Corridor Plan area is nearly built out. 
In October 2024, MidPen Housing Corporation (MidPen Housing) acquired 2000 Delaware adjacent to its 
existing Delaware Pacific property. The two sites share a parking structure, community room, fitness center, 
and common area. A single trip generation threshold applies to the two adjacent properties. MidPen 
Housing has renamed the newly acquired property “Delaware Atlantic.” Delaware Pacific and Delaware 
Atlantic together provide 120 units of below-market-rate (BMR) housing.  
Data collection for the 2024 annual monitoring of the TMA was completed on October 17, 2024. The trip 
generation counts indicated that all projects except one were at or below their short-term thresholds. One 
project, Delaware Pacific-2000 Delaware, generated 67 PM peak-hour vehicle trips, exceeding its short-
term threshold 52. The count for Azara, 24 PM peak-hour trips, was one trip shy of its short-term threshold.  
Compared to the 2023 counts, the 2024 TMA trip counts indicated a slight increase in trip generation at 
the 400/450 Concar project and a substantial reduction in office trip generation at the Franklin Templeton 
complex due to its tenant, Roblox, relocating to Station 5 in Bay Meadows Phase II. The 2024 trip counts 
indicated increased residential trip generation at Delaware Pacific-2000 Delaware and Station Park Green, 
and little or no changes at the other three projects. Finally, it is essential to note that trip generation counts 
at three of the five residential projects (Peninsula Station, Delaware Pacific-2000 Delaware, and Azara) were 
higher than their long-term trip reduction goals. The TMA and the members have discussed long-term trip 
reduction goals and understand the implications for the future. 
Although the Delaware Pacific-2000 Delaware project has exceeded the short-term trip threshold for the 
last four years, the project team has consistently collaborated with the City to implement TDM strategies 
aimed at reducing trips. Now that MidPen Housing owns both properties, there is an opportunity to review 
the combined travel behavior, trip generation, and TDM aspects with the City when considering necessary 
strategies to reduce site trip generation. 
Trip generation for Bay Meadows Phase II was evaluated according to the monitoring requirement outlined 
in the Traffic Management Plan for Bay Meadows Phase II. Data was collected on Thursday, October 17, 
2024, using Automated License Plate Recognition (ALPR) cameras. The resulting trip generation was 2,454 
PM peak-hour vehicle trips, approximately 85% of the maximum trip threshold (2,878 PM peak-hour vehicle 
trips) allowed under the Conditions of Approval (COA) for the mid-term stage.  
After several years of experience, collaboration between the TMA and the City, and diligent work by the TMA 
and its traffic counting team, the trip generation monitoring procedure is well adapted to the complexities 
of the Bay Meadows Phase II study area and meets the intent and guidelines of the Corridor Plan in content 
and results. With careful deployment and execution, it should continue to provide confident results.

--- page 208 ---
ii 
 
During entitlement, all TMA member projects were required to develop TDM or trip reduction plans that 
reflected the City's guiding documents and practices. Relevant documents were reviewed to document trip 
reduction thresholds and TDM or trip reduction strategies. Bicycle parking, transit provisions, and commute 
coordination were cited most often in these documents. 
Similar to past years, TMA members completed a survey developed to solicit feedback about current TDM 
practices. Responses were received from member representatives of 11 completed projects, and essential 
facts about TDM and trip reduction practices, including management, specific programs offered, 
distribution of TDM information, and surveying travel behavior, were included in the responses. Since its 
implementation in 2020, this survey exercise has provided a qualitative overview of TDM practices. The 
annual report has focused solely on vehicle trip generation to determine project compliance. Actual TDM 
Plan compliance has not been addressed and remains the responsibility of each project under its respective 
COA.

1 
 
This report details the results of vehicle trip monitoring conducted under the San Mateo Rail Corridor 
Transit-Oriented Development Plan (Corridor Plan). It also presents a qualitative overview of Transportation 
Demand Management (TDM) plans for completed projects in the Rail Corridor area and a summary of the 
results of a San Mateo Rail Corridor Transportation Management Association (TMA) members’ survey. 
Background 
In 2005, the City of San Mateo (City) adopted the Corridor Plan. The plan's stated goal is to allow, 
encourage, and provide guidance for the creation of world-class transit-oriented development (TOD) within 
a half-mile radius of the Hillsdale and Hayward Park Caltrain station areas while maintaining and improving 
the quality of life for those who already live and work in the area.  
The Corridor Plan included a framework for the creation of TOD, implementation of a TDM program that 
generates an overall reduction in new vehicle trips of at least 25% corridor-wide, establishment of trip 
generation thresholds, establishment of parking standards, and monitoring of trip generation. The Corridor 
Plan also called for the creation of the TMA. It stipulated that participation in the TMA was required for all 
new development within the TOD zone, strongly encouraged for all new development within the broader 
Corridor Plan area, and available to any existing uses outside the Corridor Plan area (Policy 7.18).  
The City adopted the Hillsdale Station Area Plan (Station Plan) in 2011. The area addressed in the Station 
Plan was based on the site within walking distance of the now-relocated Hillsdale Caltrain Station. The 
Station Plan expanded the TMA formed under the Corridor Plan to include all properties within the Station 
Plan area and required all new developments to join the TMA. It stated that Hillsdale Shopping Center’s 
participation in the TMA will consist of optional measures and will not be subject to the TMA’s trip reduction 
goals (Policy TRA-4.2). 
Figure 1 illustrates the Corridor Plan and Station Plan areas. 
Purpose of the TMA 
As defined in its bylaws, the TMA aims to implement the Objectives of the Corridor Plan. Within the Corridor 
Plan area, the TMA provides the following functions. 
• 
Oversee TDM program implementation. 
• 
Arrange shared parking, as appropriate. 
• 
Market TDM services and programs. 
• 
Coordinate TDM services and programs. 
• 
Coordinate with the City on annual trip generation monitoring for completed projects. 
• 
Participate in the annual report to the San Mateo City Council about information on development 
trip generation. 
• 
Consult with non-compliant members about changes to their TDM programs if trip generation 
goals are unmet. The intent here is to support members, not enforce project COA related to trip 
reduction goals, which only the City is authorized to do.  
• 
Outside the Corridor Plan area, the TMA may coordinate with other agencies. 
The TMA does not currently fund TDM services or programs. Member projects with active TDM programs 
do so at their own expense, independently, or in partnership with other members or Commute.org.

2024 TMA Activities 
Official TMA meetings were held virtually, using the Zoom platform, in January (General Membership and 
Board of Directors), May, and September 2024. The TMA directors, officers, and contacts, as well as 
meeting minutes, are included in Appendix A. 
Corridor Plan Area Project Status 
Construction continued in the Corridor Plan area during the 2024 calendar year, including completion of 
apartments on Residential Block 6 and site work on Mixed-Use Blocks 3A and 3B. Figure 2 summarizes 
completed projects in the Corridor Plan area. Figure 3 summarizes future projects under construction or 
approved. By inspection, development in the Corridor Plan area is nearly complete.  
In October 2024, MidPen Housing Corporation (MidPen Housing) acquired 2000 Delaware adjacent to its 
existing Delaware Pacific property. The two sites share a parking structure, community room, fitness center, 
and common area. A single trip generation threshold applies to the two adjacent properties. MidPen 
Housing has renamed the newly acquired property “Delaware Atlantic.” Delaware Pacific and Delaware 
Atlantic together provide 120 units of below-market-rate (BMR) housing.  
Trip Generation Thresholds and TDM Measures 
During each development project’s entitlement phase, vehicle trip generation is calculated using trip 
generation rates published in the Trip Generation Manual issued by the Institute of Transportation 
Engineers (ITE). Trip reductions are calculated based on a development’s density, location, proximity to 
transit, the mix of land uses, and TDM programs. Each project’s COA establishes short-term and long-term 
trip generation thresholds that need to be met for the life of a project. Short-term goals are based on the 
varying status of completed projects within the corridor area. Long-term trip reduction goals are based on 
the full build-out of transit-oriented neighborhoods envisioned in the Corridor Plan. Many long-term goals 
are also based on the 25th Avenue Grade Separation Project, which created new roadway connections on 
28th Avenue and 31st Avenue between El Camino Real and Delaware Street. 
TMA projects must submit individual TDM plans with a list of trip-reduction strategies to be implemented 
once the project is occupied. TDM plans are tailored to reflect the project's location, proximity, and access 
to transit, walkability, proposed land uses, and other relevant factors. 
Trip Generation Monitoring 
Scope of Study 
The TMA is required to collect data annually regarding the number of vehicle trips generated by each 
development. Trip generation is determined by collecting driveway counts at all occupied projects. These 
data are compared to the allowable trip generation threshold identified in each development’s COA. All 
projects are currently required to meet their short-term trip reduction goals.

Bay Meadows Phase II Trip Generation 
Trip generation for Bay Meadows Phase II was evaluated according to the monitoring requirement outlined in the 
Traffic Management Plan for Bay Meadows Phase II. Data was collected on Thursday, October 17, 2024, using 
Automated License Plate Recognition (ALPR) cameras. The procedures and results of this monitoring effort are 
presented below. 
Previous Driveway Counts and Maximum Trip Threshold 
Before 2019, the City conducted annual driveway counts at each block within Bay Meadows Phase II as an interim 
method to gain insight into the neighborhood's trip generation. The driveway count program has proven cost-
effective and has captured most of the trips generated by Bay Meadows Phase II. The 2018 Annual Report noted 
that Bay Meadows Phase II trip generation would likely increase when the complete monitoring program is 
implemented and all trips, including vehicles that park on the street, are counted.  
Bay Meadows Phase II project development is divided into four stages: one stage reflecting pre-grade separation 
conditions and three stages of post-grade separation reflecting short-term (Phase I), mid-term (Phase II), and long-
term (Phase III) conditions. For the post-grade separation stages, trip generation goals were set as follows: 10% 
short-term, 16% mid-term, and 25% long-term reduction. The trip reduction goal was determined based on the 
grade separation project and the overall development completed.  
Bay Meadows Phase II is currently in the mid-term (Phase II) post-grade separation stage of development after the 
completion of the 25th Avenue Grade Separation Project, based on the COA. Also, per the COA, the mid-term trip 
reduction goal for this stage is 16% of the total PM peak hour ITE trip generation for completed projects. The 
maximum trip threshold for the mid-term stage is 2,878 PM peak-hour vehicle trips.  
Estimated Trip Generation in 2024 
Cordon and Gateways 
The Traffic Management Plan defined six area access points, or gateways, used by vehicles entering and leaving 
the Bay Meadows Phase II area (Study Area). Figure 6 illustrates the Study Area and gateways listed below (coded 
by origin - O1 through O6). 
• 
O1 – South Delaware Street north of East 28th Avenue 
• 
O2 – South Delaware Street south of Lopez Drive 
• 
O3 – 28th Avenue west of Delaware Street  
• 
O4 – East 28th Avenue west of Saratoga Drive 
• 
O5 – 31st Avenue west of Delaware Street  
• 
O6 – Franklin Parkway east of Baze Road 
Figure 7 shows the typical travel paths associated with each gateway. 
Two driveways on South Delaware Street just inside the Study Area generate traffic unrelated to the area's 
development. One serves the Event Center, and the other serves the City’s Clean Water project construction site. 
Counts were conducted at these two locations to exclude this traffic from the Study Area traffic.

13 
 
Cordon Counts 
The ALPR cameras were deployed for two-hour cordon counts and peak hour license plate surveys of weekday 
vehicle traffic entering and leaving the Study Area on Thursday, October 17, 2024, between 4:00 PM and 6:00 PM. 
Figure 7 summarizes the peak period cordon counts, and Figure 8 presents the peak hour cordon counts, which 
were approximately 55% of the peak period values. The license plate surveys recorded license plate numbers and 
entry/exit times for every vehicle entering and leaving each gateway. These were tabulated to identify and sum 
travel times for every car registered at two gateways during the peak hour, resulting in peak hour “paired vehicle 
trips” for each gateway. 
Estimated Through Trips 
The travel times for all paired vehicle trips traversing typical paths between entry and exit gateways were examined 
to estimate through trips. This involved comparing average travel times, presented in Figure 9, and maximum travel 
times, presented in Figure 10, to capture outlier travel times indicating stops within the Study Area. Paired trips 
with travel times exceeding the average by more than 1 to 2 minutes, depending on the distance between gateways 
and the number of traffic signals along the route, were considered to have stopped within the Study Area. As a 
result, approximately 8% of all paired trips were not considered through trips. Figure 11 presents the gateway-to-
gateway trip matrix, and Figure 12 summarizes trips entering and leaving the Study Area by gateway. 
Estimated PM Peak Hour Trip Generation 
Approximately 4,938 PM peak-hour vehicle trips were counted entering and leaving the Study Area. This value 
includes all vehicle trips—those that originated in or were destined for points within the Study Area, those that 
passed through the Study Area, and those generated by the Event Center (0 trips) and the Clean Water project 
construction site (6 PM peak-hour vehicle trips).  
As presented below, the estimated PM peak-hour trip generation was derived from the difference between the 
cordon counts and the sum of through-vehicle trips and other vehicle trips not associated with Study Area 
development. 
• 
Trips Entering and Leaving: 
4,938 
• 
Less Trips Not Associated: 
        6 
• 
SUBTOTAL TRIPS: 
 
4,932 
• 
LESS THROUGH TRIPS:  
2,478 
• 
TRIP GENERATION: 
 
2,454 
• 
TRIP THRESHOLD: 
 
2,878 
The 2024 PM peak-hour trip generation is approximately 85% of the maximum trip threshold allowed under the 
COA for the mid-term stage and an increase of 276 peak-hour vehicle trips over the 2023 figure of 2,178 peak-hour 
vehicle trips (13% increase).  
Observations 
After several years of experience, collaboration between the TMA and the City, and diligent work by the TMA and its 
traffic counting team, the trip generation monitoring procedure is well adapted to the complexities of the Bay 
Meadows Phase II study area and meets the intent and guidelines of the Corridor Plan in content and results. With 
careful deployment and execution, it should continue to provide confident results.

Project TDM Plans 
This section presents a qualitative overview of member project TDM or trip reduction plans.  
TDM Plans 
All projects were required, during entitlement, to develop TDM or trip reduction plans to reflect City guiding 
documents and practice. The following documents were reviewed for this report. 
• 
1650 S. Delaware Street Final Transportation Demand Management Plan (Hexagon Transportation 
Consultants, Inc., July 18, 2018) [Azara] 
• 
2000 Delaware Trip Reduction Program and Trip Generation Threshold (Nelson\Nygaard 
Consulting Associates, Memorandum, February 9, 2011) [also covers Delaware Pacific] 
• 
92 and Delaware Trip Reduction Plan (Nelson\Nygaard Consulting Associates, Memorandum, 
February 9, 2011) [400/450 Concar] 
• 
Bay Meadows Phase II Traffic Management Plan (Kimley Horn, Latest Revision: August 24, 2018) 
• 
Franklin Templeton Campus Expansion Transportation Impact Analysis (Hexagon Transportation 
Consultants, Inc., June 8, 2017) 
• 
2090 South Delaware Trip Reduction Program (Nelson\Nygaard Consulting Associates, 
Memorandum, April 30, 2012) [Mode] 
• 
2901 - 2905 El Camino Real TDM and Trip Reduction Program (Nelson\Nygaard Consulting 
Associates, Memorandum, April 10, 2008) [Peninsula Station] 
• 
Station Park Green TDM Program – Final Plan (Nelson\Nygaard Consulting Associates, 
Memorandum, May 30, 2010) 
• 
Conditions of Approval, PA 12-051, The Nueva High School SPAR (the City of San Mateo, Approved 
by the Planning Commission on December 11, 2012) 
While respective TDM or trip reduction requirements for projects within Bay Meadows Phase II were 
defined in its Traffic Management Plan, one such project, The Nueva School, prepared a transportation 
management plan to provide additional details for the school operation.  
Figure 13 provides an overview of trip reduction thresholds defined in TDM or trip reduction plans for 
completed projects.

Survey of Members 
The above information provided a good overview of what TDM or trip reduction programs were established 
for member projects during entitlement. Similar to past years, a brief survey of TMA members was 
developed to solicit feedback about current practices. One member, 2000 Delaware, did not participate 
this year due to the aforementioned change in ownership in October 2024.  
The survey covered the following points. 
• 
Nueva School faculty, staff, and student counts 
• 
Residential project count and occupancy (percent) 
• 
Commercial project occupancy (percent), employee count, and current tenants 
• 
Management of TDM programs and activities 
• 
TDM program management 
• 
TDM programs and amenities currently offered 
• 
TDM programs that are most effective in reducing drive-alone vehicle trips 
• 
TDM program information distribution methods 
• 
Use of surveys regarding travel behaviors  
• 
Metrics used to track the performance of TDM programs 
• 
Construction or roadway work that may have impacted project access 
• 
Comments or experiences related to TDM 
Responses were received from member representatives of all 12 completed projects. They revealed 
essential facts about TDM and trip reduction practices, summarized below. Appendix B includes a summary 
of survey responses, excluding contacts and irrelevant information. 
Occupancy 
Residential occupancy was high—above 90 percent. In 2023, two properties were just below 90 percent – 
Azara at 85 percent and 2000 Delaware at 88 percent. 
Commercial occupancy decreased at Franklin Templeton (from 90 percent in 2023 to 40 percent in 2024). 
It increased at Bay Meadows Commercial (from 45 percent to 95 percent), primarily due to Roblox's 
relocation from Franklin Templeton to Bay Meadows Commercial. Occupancy at 400/450 Concar increased 
from 75% in 2023 to 80% in 2024. 
TDM Program Management 
Six members reported in-house management; three noted they do not provide TDM programming. One 
indicated that tenants were responsible for managing their own TDM programs. 
TDM Programs and Amenities 
The following points summarize member-reported programs in place.  
• 
Ten members offered secure bicycle storage and bicycle racks. A few members provided related 
features like bike share, bicycle repair, safety education, and shower facilities. 
• 
Seven members offered electric vehicle (EV) charging stations, which are now required by code. 
• 
Four members offered transit provisions, including subsidized transit passes and shuttle programs. 
Two members reported that Commute.org shuttles served their property. Four members reported 
227 of 349

--- page 228 ---
20 
 
commute coordination efforts related to on-site transportation information and emergency rides 
home. 
• 
Two members offered amenities that support delivery services.  
• 
One member offered no TDM programs or amenities. 
Figure 14 presents an overview of current programs by project. While the array of reported strategies 
generally aligns with the overview of TDM programs summarized on page 17, this qualitative overview did 
not include a detailed project-by-project comparison.  
Most-Effective Programs 
Members’ responses to the question about programs most effectively reducing drive-alone trips are 
summarized below. 
• 
Bike racks (4 responses) 
• 
Secure bike storage (3 responses) 
• 
Fully-subsidized transit passes (3 responses) 
• 
Delivery amenities (2 responses) 
• 
EV charging stations (2 responses) 
• 
Commute.org shuttle (2 responses) 
• 
Employer-sponsored shuttle (1 response) 
Distribution of TDM Program Information 
 
Eight members indicated they distributed information to their populations using email, bulletin boards or 
kiosks, internal websites, social media, lease or information documents, or face-to-face gatherings. Three 
members reported they do not distribute information. 
Surveys on Travel Behaviors 
Just one member indicated they surveyed their populations about travel behaviors, but five members 
indicated they planned to in the future. Five members reported they do not plan to do so. 
Tracking Performance of TDM Programs 
Six members tracked performance – three used parking utilization, and three used program participation. 
Five members did not track performance. 
Comments About Impacts of Construction/Roadway Work 
One member noted that construction work on South Delaware Street and Saratoga Drive impacted access 
to their property. 
Additional Comments  
One member noted that many tenants used food and product delivery services, which reduced related 
external car trips as desired. Still, these delivery trips were counted as project trips, thereby distorting their 
trip-reduction efforts. 
Observations 
Since its implementation in 2020, this survey exercise has provided a qualitative overview of TDM practices. 
The annual report has focused solely on vehicle trip generation to determine project compliance. Actual 
228 of 349

21 
 
TDM Plan compliance has not been addressed and remains the responsibility of each project under its 
respective COA.

MINUTES 
SAN MATEO RAIL CORRIDOR TMA 
General Membership & Board of Directors Meeting 
 
January 22, 2024, 11:00 AM 
Online (Zoom) 
 
Present: 
Mike Wiley – PAP (2000 Delaware) 
Dave Wilber – Four Corners Properties (Azara) 
 
 
Adam Hamilton – Wilson Meany (Bay Meadows) 
Sarah Etheredge – MidPen Housing (Delaware Pacific) 
 
 
Kyle Deshon – Sares Regis (Mode) 
 
 
Tiffany Eng – Bridge Housing (Montara) 
 
 
 
 
Rebecca Barnes – MidPen Housing (Peninsula Station) 
Brad Underwood – City of San Mateo 
Christian Diggs – Diamond Properties (400/450 Concar) 
 
Staff:  
John Ford – Commute.org 
 
Guests: 
Carmen Chen – Commute.org 
 
Absent:  
Franklin Templeton 
 
Nueva School 
Station Park Green 
 
 
 
1. Call to Order 
• 
The meeting was called to order by Chair Sarah Etheredge at 11:04 AM. 
 
2. Approvals 
• 
On a motion/second by Adam/Rebecca, the meeting minutes of September 11, 2023, 
were approved as presented. 
3. Project Updates 
• 
Bay Meadows (Adam) reported that Station 1 and 5 have ongoing tenant improvements 
and RES 6 expected to receive TCO in the next couple of weeks. 
• 
All other projects reported status quo conditions since the last meeting in September 
2023. 
 
4. City of San Mateo Update 
• 
Brad reported that bike facility improvements are planned along 28th Avenue across El 
Camino Real. The project was presented to the Planning Commission in December 2023. 
• 
There is also an ongoing effort for bike lanes along Delaware from Concar to 28th Avenue. 
5. Report from Acting Executive Director (John Ford) 
• 
John reviewed the financial statements for the period ending December 31, 2023. On a 
motion/second by Rebecca/Adam, the statements were accepted as presented. 
• 
John told the group that the TMA taxes for 2023 would be filed soon now that the 
financial year is complete.  
239 of 349

--- page 240 ---
Page 2 of 3 
 
6. 2023 Counts and Annual Report 
• 
John gave the group an overview of the driveway and cordon counts that were conducted 
on October 17, 2023, and reviewed the report provided by Hexagon Transportation 
Consultants who managed the count subconsultant and analyzed count data. Paul 
Krupka also assisted with the count methodology due to the change in consultant from 
IDAX, the previous count consultant. 
• 
Automatic license plate readers (ALPRs) were used to capture license plates of vehicles 
entering and leaving the cordon area. Actual travel times were then compared to Google 
estimated travel times to determine the number of through trips. 
• 
Hexagon informed us that the use of ALPRs requires a significant amount of human 
analysis to determine the through-trip analysis. Their subcontractor absorbed the cost 
overruns for the 2023 count but will likely increase their costs for future counts. Hexagon 
has suggested using Streetlight data in 2024 as a more cost-effective option. Tube 
counts would still be used for driveways and entry/exit locations, but historical data 
would be used to calculate through trips. John will follow up with Sue-Ellen Atkinson (City 
of San Mateo) to determine if this is a possibility for future counts. 
• 
John shared the proposal from Krupka Consulting for creating the 2023 Annual Report 
and providing consulting assistance with the 2024 counts. 
• 
Carmen reported that the annual TMA survey was sent via email to all members in 
November 2023. All members completed the survey, and Paul will include the responses 
in the 2023 Annual Report. 
• 
John said we are looking to present the 2023 report to Sustainability & Infrastructure 
Commission in early Spring and will let the members know when a date has been 
confirmed. 
 
7. New Business 
• 
Election of New Directors 
o On a motion/second by Adam/Tiffany, the slate of directors was approved as 
presented with no changes. 
• 
Election of Officers 
o On a motion/second by Adam/Tiffany, the slate of officers was approved as 
presented with no changes: 
 
Sarah Etheredge, Chair 
 
Adam Hamilton, Vice Chair 
 
Nael Younes, Secretary/Treasurer 
• 
Budget/Dues Discussion and Approval 
o John presented a draft budget for 2024 which included expenditures for the 
consultant’s production of the 2023 annual report plus estimated expenses for 
the consultant to oversee the 2024 counts (Krupka proposal), estimated costs 
for 2024 study counts (Hexagon estimate), up to 60 hours of 
admin/management time, insurance, and miscellaneous expenses. At the 
direction of the membership, nothing was budgeted for TDM (Transportation 
Demand Management) programming in 2024. 
o The 2024 budget estimates Hexagon’s work at $32,000, mirroring the 2023 
cost. This is due to the uncertainty of costs, which depend on the City’s approval 
of a different cordon count methodology such as the use of Streetlight data. 
240 of 349

--- page 241 ---
Page 3 of 3 
 
o Krupka Consulting’s costs will be lower in 2024 than 2023 because Hexagon 
took a larger role in data analysis and reporting. 
o The increased cost of conducting the driveway and cordon counts in 2023 meant 
that the TMA had to use reserves to cover annual expenses. With a comparable 
situation likely in 2024, the Executive Committee recommended a 3% increase in 
dues. While the TMA will still operate at a deficit, the dues increase will raise 
revenue by $3,000. This is the first change to dues since 2017. 
o Tiffany asked how deficits were covered in previous years. John responded that 
the TMA generated reserves in the past, which is currently covering the deficit. 
Sarah reminded the membership that the deficit may be less if the city approves 
a count methodology that is less costly. 
o Revenue for the budget was forecast using the updated dues structure. Revenue 
will increase modestly in 2024 due to more projects being part of the TMA and 
more residential and commercial projects becoming eligible for inclusion in the 
dues structure.  
o The proposed budget would result in an $8,522 deficit and leave reserves of 
approximately $38,000 at year end.  
o Dues invoices will be generated and sent to all members in February.  Adjusting 
invoices (if necessary) will be generated and sent later in the year for projects 
that receive their Certificate of Occupancy mid-year. Those dues will be pro-rated 
based on the COO date. 
o On a motion/second by Adam/Tiffany, the 2024 budget, dues increase, and 
Proposal for Consultant Services from Paul Krupka was approved as presented. 
Dues for 2024 were set as follows:  
Dues Category 
2023 Rate 
Residential rate per unit 
 $ 6.18 
Commercial rate per rentable square foot 
 $ 0.0232  
Educational rate per square foot of buildings 
 $ 0.0077  
 
• 
No other new business was discussed. 
 
8. Adjournment 
 
 
• 
The meeting adjourned at 11:52 AM.

MINUTES 
SAN MATEO RAIL CORRIDOR TMA 
Board of Directors Meeting 
 
May 13, 2024, 11:00 AM 
Online (Zoom) 
 
 
Present: 
Tiffany Eng – Bridge Housing (Montara) 
Christian Diggs – Diamond Properties (400/450 Concar) 
David Wilbur – Four Corners Properties (Azara) 
Mike Wiley – PAP (2000 Delaware) 
 
 
Nael Younes – Franklin Templeton 
Sarah Etheredge – MidPen Housing (Delaware Pacific) 
 
 
Jason Pechar – Essex (Station Park Green) 
 
Staff:  
John Ford – Commute.org 
 
Guests: 
Matt Fabry – City of San Mateo 
Carmen Chen – Commute.org 
 
 
Absent:  
Bay Meadows 
 
 
Peninsula Station 
 
 
Nueva School 
 
 
Mode 
 
 
1. Call to Order 
• 
The meeting was called to order by TMA Chair Sarah Etheredge at 11:03 AM. 
 
2. Project & TMA Area Updates 
• 
All projects reported status quo conditions since the last meeting in January 2024. 
• 
Matt shared that the City is conducting outreach for the Delaware Street Safe Routs to 
School Corridor Bicycle Improvements Project. Outreach efforts include putting signage 
along the corridor, conducting an online survey, and holding pop-up events. 
• 
Matt also shared that the proposed citywide TDM ordinance is going to City Council on 
May 20, 2024. He clarified that the new TDM ordinance would only apply to new 
development projects, not existing ones such as those in the TMA. 
• 
John reminded members that Commute.org offers bike education workshops for the 
commuter population. Commercial properties interested in hosting may contact 
Commute.org. 
 
3. Review & Approvals 
• 
Christian requested for the meeting minutes of January 22, 2024 to indicate he was 
present. Staff will correct the meeting minutes. 
• 
On a motion/second by Nael/Tiffany, the meeting minutes of January 22, 2024, were 
approved as presented pending the update. 
242 of 349

--- page 243 ---
Page 2 of 2 
 
4. Report from Acting Executive Director (John Ford) 
• 
John reviewed the financial statements for the period ending April 30, 2024. On a 
motion/second by Nael/Tiffany, the statements were accepted as presented. 
• 
John provided administrative updates which included the takeover of First Republic Bank 
by JP Morgan Chase, insurance renewals, and tax filings. Because the TMA’s taxable 
income is less than $50,000, a full tax return was not required for 2023. That will 
change once revenue exceeds $50,000. 
 
5. New Business 
• 
2023 Annual Report 
o John shared the presentation for the 2023 Annual Report that was given to the 
City’s Sustainability and Infrastructure Committee (S&I Committee) on May 8, 
2024.  
o The annual report was compiled by Krupka Consulting and includes findings from 
driveway and cordon counts conducted in October by Hexagon Transportation 
Consultants, and the annual TMA survey. 
o The cordon counts showed that Bay Meadows was below its short-term trip 
threshold. 
o Delaware Pacific/2000 Delaware were above their short-term threshold but did 
perform better than the previous year. All other projects were below their short-
term threshold. 
o John shared that the S&I Committee unanimously recommended City Council 
acceptance of the annual report. For subsequent reports, the Committee 
requested a more in-depth analysis of the annual survey that includes a year-
over-year comparison. The Committee also expressed concern on whether the 
long-term thresholds for each project will be achievable. 
o Sarah confirmed that the S&I Committee focused on data and anticipates similar 
questions in the future. 
o Mike asked when the annual report will be presented to City Council for 
acceptance. Matt shared that he would confirm the date, and John will notify the 
Board upon confirmation. 
o Matt shared that the S&I Committee were also interested in financial penalties 
related to compliance of the new TDM ordinance. He clarified that they would not 
apply to the TMA. 
• 
Counts/Annual Report 2024 
o John shared that the TMA hopes to continue contracting with Hexagon 
Transportation Consultants for the 2024 driveway and cordon counts. He 
reminded members that IDAX, the previous consultant, had opted out of 
performing counts due to technology limitations. 
o Following the 2023 counts, Hexagon suggested using a different technology and 
data set other than automatic license plate readers (ALPRs) for the cordon 
counts at Bay Meadows. This suggestion will need to be explored by the City, the 
consultant, and Bay Meadows. 
o John confirmed that the annual TMA survey will be updated based on suggestions 
from the S&I Committee. 
• 
No other new business was reported. 
 
8. Adjournment 
 
 
• 
The meeting adjourned at 11:44 AM.
