MINUTES 
SAN MATEO RAIL CORRIDOR TMA 
Board of Directors Meeting 
 
September 9, 2024, 11:00 AM 
Online (Zoom) 
 
Present: 
Ali Ghatala – Essex (Station Park Green) 
Adam Hamilton – Wilson Meany (Bay Meadows) 
David Wilbur – Four Corners Properties (Azara) 
Kyle Deshon – Sares Regis (Mode) 
Mike Wiley – PAP (2000 Delaware) 
 
 
Nael Younes – Franklin Templeton 
Rebecca Barnes – MidPen Housing (Peninsula Station) 
Sarah Etheredge – MidPen Housing (Delaware Pacific) 
Matt Fabry – City of San Mateo 
 
Absent:  
400/450 Concar 
Montara 
Nueva School 
 
Staff:  
John Ford – Commute.org 
 
Guests: 
Jay Yu – City of San Mateo 
Jason Pechar– Essex (Station Park Green) 
 
 
Carmen Chen – Commute.org 
 
 
 
1. Call to Order 
• 
The meeting was called to order by TMA Chair Sarah Etheredge at 11:02 AM. 
 
2. Roll Call & Introductions 
• 
John conducted a roll call. 
• 
Ali Ghatala (Essex) and Jay Yu (City of San Mateo) introduced themselves. 
• 
Jay shared that Sue-Ellen is no longer with the City of San Mateo and he and Matt will be 
covering her role until they backfill the position in the coming weeks. 
 
3. Project Updates & TMA Area Updates 
• 
Jay shared three bicycle/pedestrian projects that are in the design phase. 
o Delaware Street: The City is 95% complete with the design phase of a Class IV 
bike lane and bike boulevard on Delaware Street. The project will not remove any 
existing vehicle lanes and will improve overall connectivity in the Rail Corridor 
area. 
o 28th Avenue Gap Closure: The project will provide a safe path of travel for 
pedestrians and bicyclists crossing El Camino Real at 28th Avenue. 
o 19th Avenue: This project is entering the design phase and will result in a Class 
IV bike facility on 19th Avenue from Pacific Boulevard to Mariners Island 
Boulevard. 
• 
Adam asked when the Delaware Street and 28th Ave projects would be complete. 
244 of 349

--- page 245 ---
Page 2 of 3 
 
o Jay responded that the Delaware Street project will be complete in Summer 
2025, and the 28th Avenue Gap Closure completion is uncertain. 
• 
Bay Meadows (Adam) shared that Res 6 is open. Most activity is on the office side, with 
Roblox in Station 2, and SurveyMonkey moving out of Station 4. They also have approved 
plans for the last two undeveloped sites. 
• 
All remaining projects reported status quo conditions since the last meeting in May 
2024. 
 
4. Approvals 
• 
On a motion/second by Adam/Rebecca, the meeting minutes of May 13, 2024, were 
approved as presented. 
5. Report from Acting Executive Director (John Ford) 
• 
John reviewed the financial statements for the period ending August 31, 2024. On a 
motion/second by Adam/Nael, the statements were accepted as presented. 
• 
John provided administrative updates which included insurance renewal, and the 
stakeholder contact list (TMA members should indicate any updates),  
 
6. New Business 
• 
Counts/Annual Report 2024 
o John reviewed the requirements and protocols for conducting annual traffic 
counts at all member locations. 
o John shared that the TMA received a proposal from Hexagon, the previous year’s 
count consultant. The proposal is $25,000 for the 2024 counts, as opposed to 
the same scope of work that was completed for $32,000 last year. Following the 
2023 counts, Hexagon raised concerns regarding the amount of manual 
verification needed to verify travel times for cordon counts. Hexagon explored 
other options, including Bluetooth sensors, and ultimately concluded that the 
same count methodology would be best. John noted that any future modifications 
to count methodology will be subject to review and approval by the City. 
o Sarah asked whether the TMA had previously increased the count budget to 
account for the potential increase in cost for the 2024 counts. 
 
John verified that the budget was not increased due to uncertainties with 
the count methodology. 
o Adam asked for clarity on the county methodology and whether the cost 
increased due to the manual verification needed. 
 
John confirmed that the methodology is the same as last year’s and 
would be completed at a lower cost. 
o Matt shared that the Event Center will likely keep the driveway that is currently 
one of the count locations, for large events. 
 
John replied that future counts will continue to be conducted at that 
location so that this traffic can be excluded from the Study Area traffic. 
o On a motion/second by Adam/Nael, the proposal from Hexagon was unanimously 
accepted as presented. The board instructed John to proceed with contracting 
Hexagon for the project.

• 
Review Meeting Dates for 2025 
o John shared the calendar for meetings in 2025. The next meeting will be on 
Monday, January 13, 2025. John will distribute the meeting calendars via 
Outlook invitation.  
• 
No other new business was discussed. 
 
8. Adjournment 
 
 
• 
The meeting adjourned at 11:39 AM.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  10
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 10-4662
File ID: 25-10614
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
December 01, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Bermuda Drive Bridge Replacement Project — Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Valentine Corporation in the amount of $6,888,369 for construction of the Bermuda Drive 
Bridge Replacement Project and establish a contingency reserve of $690,000; affirm a requested bid relief from Joseph J. 
Albanese, Inc.; approve an agreement with Biggs Cardosa Associates, Inc. in the amount of $696,000 for engineering 
design support during construction and establish a contingency reserve of $70,000; and authorize the Public Works 
Director to execute the agreements in substantially the form presented and issue change orders as allowed by the contract 
documents within the respective contingency amounts.
BACKGROUND:
In 2008, the City applied for preliminary engineering funds through the Highway Bridge Replacement and Rehabilitation 
Program (HBRRP) to evaluate the condition of the Bermuda Drive Bridge over Borel Creek and address structural 
deficiencies identified by the California Department of Transportation (Caltrans). Following approval of HBRRP funding in 
2010, the City entered into an agreement with Biggs Cardosa Associates, Inc. (BCA) for preliminary engineering. Structural 
and seismic evaluations completed in 2011-2012 recommended full bridge replacement rather than retrofit. Caltrans 
subsequently approved the revised project scope in 2017.
On May 21, 2018, City Council approved a professional services agreement for final design and environmental 
documentation with BCA. Design was completed in early 2025. The project will reconstruct the deficient bridge to provide 
a safe and reliable route consistent with current design standards.
Due to limited in-house staffing resources to oversee construction and ensure compliance with federal and Caltrans 
requirements, the City issued separate Requests for Proposals (RFPs) in September 2025 – one for inspection and materials 
testing services, and another for engineering design services during construction (ESDC). These services are necessary to 
provide daily inspection, materials testing, and engineering oversight throughout construction. Proposals were evaluated 
based on qualifications and relevant experience. Staff will be bringing the inspection and material testing services 
agreement to City Council in January for approval. 
Agreement with Valentine Corporation
In accordance with Municipal Code section 3.60.030 and federal procurement processes listed in 2 Code of Federal 
Regulations (CFR) Part 200, specifically §§ 200.317-200.327, a competitive public process was used to obtain construction 
bids for Bermuda Drive Bridge. Bermuda Drive Bridge was advertised on September 18, 2025. On October 21, 2025, six 
bids were received. The bids received are listed below in order of increasing bid amount.
271 of 349

--- page 272 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Contractor
Base Bid
Joseph J. Albanese, Inc. 
$5,063,016.00
Graniterock
$6,087,347.00
Valentine Corporation
$6,888,369.00
Ghilotti Construction Company
$7,073,366.92
Disney Construction
$7,148,333.00
Viking Construction Company
$7,998,812.00
On October 23, 2025, Joseph J. Albanese, Inc. submitted a letter requesting withdrawal (bid relief) of its bid in accordance 
with Public Contract Code Section 5100 et al. due to omission of a subcontractor listing that made the bid materially 
different than what was intended. Staff reviewed the requested bid relief, deemed the request satisfactory, approved 
Joseph J. Albanese, Inc.’s request for bid relief, and recommends for Council to affirm staff’s approval of the requested bid 
relief. 
The apparent second low bidder (Graniterock) did not submit a required Caltrans form with their bid and was determined 
to be non-responsive. Staff determined that Valentine Corporation is the lowest responsive, responsible bidder. Therefore, 
staff recommends Valentine Corporation be awarded this construction agreement. 
Construction will span two years with the first phase of construction to begin Spring 2026. 
Agreement with Biggs Cardosa Associates, Inc. (ESDC)
To provide ESDC, staff recommends awarding an agreement to Biggs Cardosa Associates, Inc., which was selected as the 
most qualified firm from the City’s September 2025 RFP. The firm’s experience with bridge design, including design of this 
bridge, makes them well qualified to provide technical assistance during construction.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The project is funded through a combination of local and federal funds under the Bermuda Drive Bridge Replacement 
Project (462250) and Federal Project No. BRLS-5102(049). These funds will be used to award the construction contract and 
consultant agreement, as well as to establish the contingency reserves.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This project is categorically exempt from CEQA it is a replacement or reconstruction of an existing structure where the new 
structure will be located on the same site as the structure replaced and will have substantially the same purpose and 
capacity as the structure replaced. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15302.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

12. Mediation. Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be 
submitted to mediation. The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request. The 
mediator shall be agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties 
shall each submit one name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, 
the California State Board of Mediation and Conciliation, or other agreed-upon service. The 
mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties. Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party. No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement. The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

Exhibit A 
Insurance Requirements for Construction Contracts
Contractor shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract, and for x years thereafter, 
insurance against claims for injuries to persons or damages to property which may arise from or in 
connection with the performance of the work hereunder by the Contractor, his agents, 
representatives, employees, or subcontractors. 
MINIMUM SCOPE AND LIMIT OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 covering CGL 
on an “occurrence” basis, including products and completed operations, property damage, bodily 
injury and personal & advertising injury with limits no less than $5,000,000 per occurrence. If a 
general aggregate limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this 
project/location (ISO CG 25 03 or 25 04) or the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required 
occurrence limit.  
2. Automobile Liability:  Insurance Services Office Form CA 0001 covering Code 1 (any auto), with 
limits no less than $5,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation insurance as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, 
and Employers’ Liability insurance with a limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Builder’s Risk (Course of Construction) insurance utilizing an “All Risk” (Special Perils) coverage 
form, with limits equal to the completed value of the project and no coinsurance penalty 
provisions.
5. Surety Bonds as described below.
6. Professional Liability (if Design/Build), with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence or 
claim, and $2,000,000 policy aggregate.
7. Contractors’ Pollution Legal Liability and/or Asbestos Legal Liability and/or Errors and Omissions 
(if project involves environmental hazards) with limits no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or 
claim, and $2,000,000 policy aggregate.
If the contractor maintains broader coverage and/or higher limits than the minimums shown above, 
the Entity requires and shall be entitled to the broader coverage and/or higher limits maintained by 
the contractor. Any available insurance proceeds in excess of the specified minimum limits of insurance 
and coverage shall be available to the Entity.
Self-Insured Retentions 
Self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the Entity. At the option of the Entity, 
either: the contractor shall cause the insurer shall to reduce or eliminate such self-insured retentions 
as respects the Entity, its officers, officials, employees, and volunteers; or the Contractor shall provide 
a financial guarantee satisfactory to the Entity guaranteeing payment of losses and related 
investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses. The policy language shall provide, or be 
endorsed to provide, that the self-insured retention may be satisfied by either the named insured or 
Entity.
Other Insurance Provisions 
281 of 349

--- page 282 ---
Construction Contract
Page 8 of 9
Rev 1/24
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
1. The Entity, its officers, officials, employees, and volunteers are to be covered as additional 
insureds on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations performed 
by or on behalf of the Contractor including materials, parts, or equipment furnished in connection 
with such work or operations and automobiles owned, leased, hired, or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the Contractor. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an endorsement to 
the Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, CG 11 85 or both CG 20 10, 
CG 20 26, CG 20 33, or CG 20 38; and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
2. For any claims related to this project, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance coverage at least as broad as ISO CG 20 01 04 13 as respects the Entity, its officers, 
officials, employees, and volunteers. Any insurance or self-insurance maintained by the Entity, 
its officers, officials, employees, or volunteers shall be excess of the Contractor’s insurance and 
shall not contribute with it. 
3. Each insurance policy required by this clause shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, 
except with notice to the Entity.
Builder’s Risk (Course of Construction) Insurance 
Contractor may submit evidence of Builder’s Risk insurance in the form of Course of Construction 
coverage. Such coverage shall name the Entity as a loss payee as their interest may appear.
If the project does not involve new or major reconstruction, at the option of the Entity, an Installation 
Floater may be acceptable. For such projects, a Property Installation Floater shall be obtained that 
provides for the improvement, remodel, modification, alteration, conversion or adjustment to existing 
buildings, structures, processes, machinery and equipment.  The Property Installation Floater shall 
provide property damage coverage for any building, structure, machinery or equipment damaged, 
impaired, broken, or destroyed during the performance of the Work, including during transit, 
installation, and testing at the Entity’s site.
Claims Made Policies – (If at all possible avoid and require occurrence type CGL policies)
If any coverage required is written on a claims-made coverage form: 
1. The retroactive date must be shown, and this date must be before the execution date of the 
contract or the beginning of contract work.
2. Insurance must be maintained and evidence of insurance must be provided for at least five (5) 
years after completion of contract work. 
3. If coverage is canceled or non-renewed, and not replaced with another claims-made policy form 
with a retroactive date prior to the contract effective, or start of work date, the Contractor must 
purchase extended reporting period coverage for a minimum of five (5) years after completion 
of contract work. 
4. A copy of the claims reporting requirements must be submitted to the Entity for review. 
5. If the services involve lead-based paint or asbestos identification/remediation, the Contractors 
Pollution Liability policy shall not contain lead-based paint or asbestos exclusions. If the services 
involve mold identification/remediation, the Contractors Pollution Liability policy shall not 
contain a mold exclusion, and the definition of Pollution shall include microbial matter, including 
mold. 
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers authorized to conduct business in the state with a current A.M. 
Best rating of no less than A: VII, unless otherwise acceptable to the Entity. 
Waiver of Subrogation 
Contractor hereby agrees to waive rights of subrogation which any insurer of Contractor may acquire

its employees, agents and subcontractors. 
Verification of Coverage 
Contractor shall furnish the Entity with original Certificates of Insurance including all required

Surety Bonds 
Contractor shall provide the following Surety Bonds:
1. Bid bond
2. Performance bond
3. Payment bond
4. Maintenance bond
The Payment Bond and the Performance Bond shall be in a sum equal to the contract price. If the 
Performance Bond provides for a one-year warranty a separate Maintenance Bond is not necessary.  If 
the warranty period specified in the contract is for longer than one year a Maintenance Bond equal to 
10% of the contract price is required.  Bonds shall be duly executed by a responsible corporate surety, 
authorized to issue such bonds in the State of California and secured through an authorized agent with 
an office in California.
Special Risks or Circumstances
Entity reserves the right to modify these requirements, including limits, based on the nature of the risk, 
prior experience, insurer, coverage, or other circumstances.

AGREEMENT WITH BIGGS CARDOSA ASSOCIATES, INC. 
FOR DESIGN PROFESSIONAL SERVICES 
FOR 
BERMUDA DRIVE BRIDGE REPLACEMENT PROJECT 
This Agreement, made and entered into this day of ____________________, by and between the CITY OF 
SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California (“CITY”), and Biggs 
Cardosa Associates, Inc., a corporation, (“CONSULTANT”), whose address is 1111 Broadway, Suite 1510 Oakland 
CA 94607: 
RECITALS: 
A. 
CITY desires certain professional engineering design services hereinafter described. 
B. 
CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these professional engineering design services by 
reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and CONSULTANT has offered to provide 
the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein. 
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows: 
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES 
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in Exhibit A 
to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference. 
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT 
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and coordination of all 
work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without additional compensation, 
correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work. 
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this Agreement. 
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform the 
services of CONSULTANT. 
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in Municipal Code 
Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer Price Index escalator. 
SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY 
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project. 
CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining thereto 
promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work. 
284 of 349

--- page 285 ---
SECTION 4 - TERM 
 
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence upon execution of agreement and 
continue until all work is completed and accepted by the City’s project manager.   
 
CITY agrees to exercise due diligence in performing its tasks to implement the CONSULTANT'S timetable. 
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT 
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment request 
upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full performance of the 
services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee, on a time and expense reimbursement 
basis, in an amount not to exceed $696,000, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this Agreement, attached 
and incorporated by reference. 
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION 
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have the right 
to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' written notice to 
CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon receipt of said written notice. 
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents become the 
property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without additional compensation. 
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS 
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although instruments of 
professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for which they are made is 
executed or not. 
SECTION 8 - CONFIDENTIALITY 
All reports and documents prepared by CONSULTANT in connection with the performance of this 
Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONSULTANT shall not make any such 
documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by CONSULTANT or CITY 
without the written consent of CITY before any such release. 
SECTION 9 - INTEREST OF CONSULTANT 
CONSULTANT covenants that it presently has no interest, and shall not acquire any interest, direct or 
indirect, financial or otherwise, which would conflict in any manner or degree with the performance of the 
services under this Agreement. 
285 of 349

--- page 286 ---
SECTION 10 - CONSULTANT'S STATUS 
 
 
It is expressly agreed that in the performance of the professional services required under this Agreement, 
CONSULTANT shall at all times be considered an independent CONSULTANT as defined in Labor Code Section 
3353, under control of the CITY as to the result of the work but not the means by which the result is 
accomplished.  Nothing herein shall be construed to make CONSULTANT an agent or employee of CITY while 
providing services under this Agreement. 
 
SECTION 11 - INDEMNITY 
 
 
CONSULTANT agrees to hold harmless and indemnify CITY, its elected and appointed officials, employees, 
and agents from and against any and all claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising out of CONSULTANT’s 
negligence, recklessness or willful misconduct to the maximum extent permitted by state law.  To the extent 
permitted by Civil Code section 2782.8, CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and appointed officials, 
employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to indemnify shall survive expiration or 
early termination of this Agreement. 
 
SECTION 12 - INSURANCE 
 
CONSULTANT shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract and three years thereafter (five 
years for building or major improvements) the insurance specified in Exhibit C to this Agreement. 
 
SECTION 13 - NONASSIGNABILITY 
 
 
Both parties hereto recognize that this Agreement is for the personal services of CONSULTANT and 
cannot be transferred, assigned, or subcontracted by CONSULTANT without the prior written consent of CITY. 
 
SECTION 14 - RELIANCE UPON PROFESSIONAL 
SKILL OF CONSULTANT 
 
 
It is mutually understood and agreed by and between the parties hereto that CONSULTANT is skilled in 
the professional calling necessary to perform the work agreed to be done under this Agreement and that CITY 
relies upon the skill of CONSULTANT to do and perform the work in the most skillful manner, and CONSULTANT 
agrees to thus perform the work.  The acceptance of CONSULTANT's work by CITY does not operate as a release 
of CONSULTANT from said obligation. 
 
SECTION 15 - WAIVERS 
 
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of 
any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such term, covenant, condition, 
ordinance or law or of any subsequent breach or violation of the same or of any other term, condition, 
ordinance, or law. The subsequent acceptance by either party of any fee or other money which may become due 
hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding breach or violation by the other party of any 
term, covenant, or condition of this Agreement or of any applicable law or ordinance. 
 
286 of 349

--- page 287 ---
SECTION 16 – SEVERABILITY 
If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise unenforceable by a 
court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall continue in full force and 
effect. 
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES 
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing of a cost 
bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.  The above 
$5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, appellate court, or otherwise, and 
regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It is the intent of this Agreement that neither 
party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to 
enforce the provisions of this Agreement. 
SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION 
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with applicable 
regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its sub-consultants shall 
discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national origin, ancestry, physical 
handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a bona fide occupational qualification 
pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act. 
SECTION 19 - MEDIATION 
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to mediation.  
The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be agreed to by the 
mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one name from mediators listed 
by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and Conciliation Service, or other agreed-
upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw. 
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the prevailing 
party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation and making a good 
faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once commenced by a meeting with the 
mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but not more than 60 days, unless the maximum 
time is extended by the parties. 
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION 
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY's request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection with 
CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or is based upon 
CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for testimony, testimony, and 
travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual testimony. 
SECTION 21 - NOTICES 
All notices hereunder shall be given in writing and mailed, postage prepaid, addressed as follows:

EXHIBIT A 
SCOPE OF SERVICES 
SCOPE OF SERVICES 
Task 1 and Task 6 – Regulatory Permit Compliance and Biological Support Services 
During the construction phase of the project, the Biggs Cardosa Team will provide technical support to assist the City 
Construction Manager with oversight of the contractor’s biologist, dewatering, storm water pollution control and other 
regulatory compliance items as needed. This may include providing interpretations of permit requirements, providing 
reviews and opinions on findings of surveys and monitoring, assisting in resolving issues including those involving CDFW, and 
other tasks that may arise. 
Section 14-6 of the project Special Provisions states that the contractor’s biologist must perform the following activities 
during construction: 
•
Certified biological monitor on-site throughout construction
•
Dewatering activities management
•
Permit review and coordination
•
Preconstruction biological and habitat surveys
•
Establishment of exclusionary zones
•
Biological awareness training
•
Provide biological monitoring and training as required by the LSAA
•
Provide nesting surveys and if required, bird deterrence prior to each mobilization
•
Provide biological monitoring/daily site checks
•
Daily monitoring of special-status habitats and species during ground disturbance or upon presence of special-status
species
•
Surface water sampling and reporting during dewatering activities
•
Routine reporting as required by the LSAA
•
Dewatering plan inspection, and reporting
We will also assist the City by reviewing technical submittals relating to regulatory compliance that the contractor prepares, 
including the following: 
•
Review Natural Resource Protection Plan
•
Stormwater Pollution Prevention Plan
During construction, we will perform the following archeological tasks to meet permit requirements: 
•
Archaeological training for each construction crews prior to ground-disturbing activity (up to 20 trainings)
•
In the event of inadvertent discovery of cultural resources, site visits to assess the nature of the finds. See Task 2 for
potential tribal consultation.
•
Reporting results of archaeological monitoring and correspondence with USACE regarding inadvertent discoveries
At the end of the construction phase, the contractor is responsible for vegetation management, trash removal and other 
permit requirement tasks for the first three years of the plant establishment period. During this period, the Biggs Cardosa 
Team will complete the following tasks. 
•
Prepare Biological As-Built Report/Final Construction Report of planting (per LSAA and USACE NWP)
•
Conduct quarterly visits and prepare Maintenance Memos to review weed control, erosion control measures, trash
removal, irrigation, etc during the first three monitoring years after the As- Built Report / Final Construction Report
(up to twelve visits)
•
Perform annual monitoring of plant cover, bank stability, plant survival rates, etc. and report to CDFW as required
by the LSAA
290 of 349

--- page 291 ---
At the end of this three year period, the construction contract and the Biggs Cardosa Team contract will be closed out and 
further plant maintenance and monitoring and reporting will transition to a new contract. 
 
Task 2 – Coordination Services 
As construction progresses, we will provide the following services as required: 
• 
Assist City staff with utility relocation coordination with PG&E Gas and CalWater 
• 
In the event of inadvertent discoveries during construction, we will coordinate directly with Native American tribes 
 
Task 3 – Clarification and Interpretation of Contract Documents 
During the construction and plant establishment periods, we will provide written responses to Requests for Information 
(RFIs) regarding technical matters, including: 
• 
Interpret design intent and technical provisions of the Contract Documents 
• 
Provide clarifications and field modifications where required by field conditions 
 
Task 4 – Review of Submittals 
Review tasks will include the following: 
• 
Provide technical review of shop drawings, product data, and material submittals, confirming general conformance 
with Contract Documents and design intent. Reviews are anticipated to typically consist of an initial review and a 
second review of the final submittal. technical design criteria and engineering judgment 
• 
Review deficiencies identified in inspection reports and test results 
• 
Complete reviews in accordance with the project schedule to minimize delays 
 
Task 5 – Construction Oversight and Field Visits 
Field visits are anticipated as follows: 
• 
Daily during pile installation and pile load testing 
• 
Visits prior to each major concrete placement (deck pours, bent caps, abutments) 
• 
Bi-weekly visits during routine construction activities 
• 
Additional visits as requested by the City or as warranted by field conditions 
 
Additional and As-Needed Tasks 
As-Built Plans: At the end of construction, as-built plans will be prepared in pdf format. In accordance with Caltrans current 
procedures, record drawings will be prepared in pdf format (not CAD) and will be based on red-marked set of plans provided 
by the contractor and records that the Biggs Cardosa Team have maintained. 
Change Orders and Corrective Actions: Change orders and engineering design to determine corrective actions due to 
materials and/or contractor's operations not meeting contract requirements may be required as construction progresses. 
When these services are required, we will provide engineering advice and technical support for construction change orders, 
including assisting City staff with preparation of change order documentation and, where appropriate, changes to plans and 
specifications. We will also provide additional field visits and engineering design to develop correction actions as required. 
Since it is not possible at this time to evaluate the level of effort and resulting cost to complete change orders, an allowance 
is included in the cost estimate. While the hours associated with this allowance are shown in the Biggs Cardosa hourly 
breakdown, these hours will be distributed to team members as required when the scope of work has been defined. No time 
will be billed to this allowance prior to our scope being identified and agreed with City staff. 
291 of 349

--- page 292 ---
Design Professional Services 2024 
 
Page 1 of 12 
Rev 1/24 
 
Key Assumptions: 
• 
Please see the attached fee breakdowns for additional assumptions regarding number of submittals, days of 
monitoring, etc. 
• 
Construction administration services will be provided by City Construction Manager and Resident Engineer 
for the project and are excluded from this scope of services. 
• 
Structural inspections, all other required inspections will be provided under a separate contract and are 
excluded from this scope of services. 
• 
Construction is assumed to be performed during the dry seasons of 2026 and 2027, with preconstruction 
activities prior to April 2026 and completion of construction in early 2028. 
• 
Our construction support services fee proposal represents our best estimate of the costs involved. The 
construction support services costs are highly dependent on the construction schedule, the contractor’s 
operations, the contractor’s proficiency and performance. For these reasons, we recommend the City include 
a contingency budget for construction support and other construction phase work, which could be used if 
more support services are required.

applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit. 
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if CONSULTANT 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease.  
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate 
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall 
be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT. 
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
Additional Insured Status 
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used). 
Primary Coverage 
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. If a Notice

Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
December 01, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Permitting Support for Citywide Creeks Maintenance Program — Appropriation and Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to appropriate $66,000 from the unassigned fund balance of the Storm Fund to the Stormwater 
Pollution operating budget; approve an agreement with Montrose Environmental Solutions, Inc. to provide professional 
consulting for the Citywide Creeks Maintenance Program in the amount of $331,987; approve a 10% contingency reserve 
in the amount of $33,200; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form 
presented and execute any future amendments within the contingency amount, including no-cost term extension 
amendments.
BACKGROUND:
Maintenance of creeks and channels within the City generally comprises vegetation management, sediment and debris 
removal, and miscellaneous routine maintenance and repair activities. Each of these activities typically requires permits 
from four or more regulatory agencies including, but not limited to, U.S. Army Corps of Engineers, California Department 
of Fish and Wildlife, California State Water Resources Control Board, U.S. Fish and Wildlife Service, National Marine 
Fisheries Service, and the Bay Conservation and Development Commission. Preparation of each of these relevant permits 
can include assessments related to biological, cultural, and tribal resources. The performance of relatively straightforward 
maintenance activities on a location-by-location basis is therefore a staff- and time-intensive effort. The City therefore 
seeks a multi-agency regulatory permit which would allow the City to operate a general maintenance program on an as-
needed basis for City-managed creeks and channels. In addition, the City is seeking a consultant to prepare a project-
specific permit for maintenance of a segment of the 16th Avenue Channel, as well as preparation of guidance which would 
be available as a resource for private property owners who are responsible for maintaining private creeks and channels 
within the City. 
On September 29, 2025, the City issued a Request for Proposals for professional consulting services to perform the 
permitting support for the Citywide Creeks Maintenance Program. Three proposals were received by the due date of 
October 30, 2025. These proposals were received by Montrose Environmental ($331,981), Nichols Consulting Engineers 
($912,105), and Soar Environmental Consulting ($430,564). After scoring the proposals based on staff knowledge and 
experience working on similar projects in the Bay Area, as well as conducting interviews of shortlisted firms, staff 
determined that Montrose Environmental Solutions, Inc. was the most qualified firm due to their technical expertise and 
relevant experience. This is a critically important effort for the City. Without receipt of regulatory permits, the City cannot 
perform necessary maintenance on creeks and channels. Staff therefore recommend awarding a professional consulting 
agreement to Montrose Environmental Solutions, Inc. The agreement term will extend from December 2025 to June 2027.
BUDGET IMPACT:
305 of 349

--- page 306 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
This work was partially budgeted in the Fiscal Year 2025-26 Stormwater Pollution operating budget in the Storm Fund, 
however, there are not sufficient funds to fully cover the anticipated cost of services planned through the end of the fiscal 
year. A supplemental budget appropriation of $66,000 from the unassigned fund balance of the Storm Fund is needed. 
Sufficient funds are available in the Storm Fund balance for this appropriation. Funding for the subsequent years of the 
agreement will be addressed through the budget development process.    
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
Approval of this agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it constitutes an administrative activity related to 
retaining professional services for environmental and regulatory permitting support that will not result in direct or indirect 
physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).) The consultant’s work will include 
preparation of CEQA documentation to evaluate potential environmental impacts of routine creek maintenance work. No 
approval of a project or commitment to a defined physical activity is being made at this time, and a separate CEQA 
determination will be made prior to any project approval. In addition, approval of a budget appropriation from an 
unassigned fund balance of the Storm Fund to the Public Works Department operating budget is exempt from CEQA 
review, because it consists of a government fiscal activity which does not involve any commitment to any specific project 
which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)

this action is categorically exempt from CEQA because it is a government fiscal activity that does

physical impact on the environment.

to the Public Works Stormwater Pollution operating budget in the Storm Fund is authorized.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Consultant shall provide the City of San Mateo with services related to obtaining all applicable Routine 
Maintenance Agreements and permits with regulatory agencies, including, but not limited to the U.S. 
Army Corps of Engineers (USACE), the Regional Water Quality Control Board (RWQCB), and California 
Fish and Wildlife (CDFW).  Permits shall provide coverage allowing for maintenance activities 
performed by the City at public waterways and by property owners of private creeks. 
At a minimum, all Proposers shall submit a proposal responding to the entire Scope of Services. 
However, Proposers may recommend changes and include alternatives to the Scope of Services if (1) 
additional tasks are required by laws or regulations, (2) tasks below are not specifically required by 
laws or regulations, or (3) tasks below can be modified to meet the City’s above-stated objectives.
A. Project Management. 
This task includes but is not limited to:
•
Developing and maintaining a master project schedule, including timelines for review of major 
deliverables
•
Leading a kick-off meeting as well as regularly scheduled meetings, including preparation of 
agendas and meeting minutes, to introduce the project strategy and schedule, and update the 
City on progress for key milestones
•
Preparing monthly progress reports and invoices 
•
Coordinating the project team, including staff and subconsultant firms, and managing all work
•
Monitoring all project activities and implementing quality assurance and quality control 
protocols and standards
•
Assembling and maintaining project files within a file sharing service that includes all 
documentation and data resulting from, or related to, the Consultant’s services for the project, 
including, but not limited to, survey files, documented assumptions, working drawings, meeting 
minutes, all correspondence, video libraries, etc.
•
Attending meetings with regulatory agencies, as necessary, to introduce or resolve items 
related to permitting
Anticipated Deliverables:
•
Project Schedule
•
Progress Reports
•
Meeting Minutes
B. Prepare Supporting Documents (Environmental Assessments, Biological Resources, Citywide 
Creeks Maintenance Plan, etc.). 
This task includes, but is not limited to:

D. Project-Specific Permit Application: 16th Ave Channel. 
The 16th Avenue Channel is identified as a priority maintenance location and the City desires to 
expedite maintenance work along a segment of this channel. With that goal in mind, the City would 
like to consider submission of a separate, stand-alone maintenance permit application specific for 
this project. This task includes preparation of the regulatory applications to allow maintenance to 
occur sooner at the 16th Avenue Channel. This segment has an abundance of Giant Reed (Arundo 
donax) growth that obstructs water flow.  Flowing eastward, this channel eventually becomes 
Leslie Creek, which feeds into the Marina Lagoon and ultimately drains into the San Francisco Bay.

E. Prepare Electronic Guidance for Property Owners of Private Creeks.  
An electronic guide document for Creekside homeowners with practical information regarding 
proper care, preventative maintenance, and if necessary, restoration of their creek bank. This 
would be targeted for creeks which are privately owned and maintained. The guide should provide 
the following:
•
Provide clear direction/guidance for what maintenance activities are permissible and what are 
not in accordance with the permit. 
•
Define the physical areas of the creek that define the limits of the maintenance actions (creek 
channel, riparian corridor, upland area).
•
Inform owner the need for permits from multiple regulatory agencies for most creek 
maintenance activities and how to apply for a permit prior to any vegetation/sediment 
removal or bank stabilization work.
•
Pruning of vegetation and limits on removal of trees.
•
Inform homeowners about causes and effects of erosion.
•
Guidance for both preventing erosion and acceptable methods for stabilizing a bank 
experiencing erosion.
•
The guidelines should be consistent with City permit conditions.
•
Provide homeowners with agency contacts and available resources.
F. Emergency Event Permitting Guidance.  
Prior to obtaining the Citywide Creeks Maintenance Permit, a storm event may be forecasted likely 
having the potential to cause significant flood damage at one or more of the priority maintenance 
locations. Using the decision criteria from the Creek Maintenance Plan (Task B) the City would 
determine whether an event qualifies as an emergency situation and would decide to act 
proactively and take action. For this task, the City seeks guidance from the consultant in identifying 
what documentation, photographic evidence, and reporting requirements are needed during and 
following the maintenance action in order to meet permit conditions as an emergency situation 
under the USACE Regional General Permit 5 (RGP-5).   
The guidance should be comprehensive to all the tasks that may be necessary to support a 
retroactive permit, which may include but not limited to:
•
Notification of Regulatory Agencies:
o
USACE District Engineer
o
California Department of Fish and Wildlife (CDFW)
o
Regional Water Quality Control Board (RWQCB)
•
San Mateo County Environmental Health Department Required Documentation
o
Maintenance Action Report

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate.
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.

Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
CONSULTANT shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies 
of the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

SUBJECT:
Basin C Sanitary Sewer Rehabilitation Project — Contingency Increase
RECOMMENDATION:
Authorize an increase to the contingency reserve associated with the construction agreement with Westland Contractors, 
Inc. for the Basin C Sanitary Sewer Rehabilitation Project in the amount of $500,000; and authorize the Public Works 
Director to issue change orders within the contingency amount. 
BACKGROUND:
The City is currently under a Cease-and-Desist Order issued by the Regional Water Quality Control Board to eliminate 
sanitary sewer overflows and unauthorized discharges of untreated or partially treated wastewater to San Francisco Bay. 
The Clean Water Program (CWP) is improving the City’s sanitary sewer system to prevent sanitary sewer overflows and 
unauthorized discharge of sewage. As part of the CWP, the annual sanitary sewer rehabilitation projects proactively 
upgrade and rehabilitate aging sewer pipes to reduce inflow and infiltration. 
Basin C includes those City areas East of Highway 101, South of J Hart Clinton Drive, and North of Foster City and Belmont. 
All Basin C sewers were evaluated using video inspection, with identified defects included in the project for repair. This 
work will ensure proper operation of the sewer collection system, reduce infiltration and inflow, and repair defects to 
prevent potential sanitary sewer overflows. The project includes the following sewer work: pipe spot repairs, full segment 
pipe replacements, rehabilitation and replacement of manholes, trenchless cured-in-place pipe spot repairs, pre- and post-
installation video inspections, and site restorations. 
On January 13, 2025, City Council awarded the Basin C construction contract to Westland Contractors, Inc. in an amount 
not to exceed $5,953,822 with a contingency reserve of $900,000 to address any unanticipated items that may arise during 
construction. Construction commenced on February 10, 2025, and is estimated to be completed by Spring 2026. 
Caltrans has an upcoming construction project which involves new paving of the public roadway on El Camino Real; the 
paving is estimated to begin in early 2026. Once El Camino Real is paved, the right of way will be under a paving 
moratorium which limits underground repair work. City staff accelerated the review of sanitary sewer video investigations 
within the Caltrans El Camino Real construction limits. As a result, several sanitary sewer main defects were identified 
which need to be repaired before Caltrans completes its paving work. This work would have normally been addressed in 
the El Camino Real and Large Diameter project, but given the timing urgency, staff evaluated whether it could be added to 
the Basin C contract.
After reviewing the proposed sewer repair work with the construction management team, City staff, contractor, and Basin 
C designer, staff executed a Change Order to use approximately $500,000 of the project contingency to complete the 
identified repairs in the El Camino Real right of way. The scope added to the Basin C project will be removed from the El 
334 of 349

--- page 335 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Camino Real & Large Diameter project. Both projects are within the same overall CWP Annual Citywide Sanitary Sewer 
Rehabilitation Project (46s091). 
To date, approximately $758,614 of the original $900,000 contingency reserve has been used for approved change orders, 
with an additional $74,183 contingency reserve identified for upcoming change orders.  To mitigate risks associated with 
potential delays, streamline project timelines, and to provide flexibility for staff to negotiate and execute contract change 
orders in a timely manner, staff recommends increasing the Basin C contingency reserve by $500,000 to offset the added 
work on El Camino Real to allow staff to issue change orders necessary to complete the Basin C project. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are available in the CWP Annual Citywide Sanitary Sewer Rehabilitation Project (46s091) to increase the 
contingency by the requested amount. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The work addressed by this administrative report is being undertaken to support the Clean Water Program. This project is 
subject to the requirements of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), the general components of which are 
included as part of the Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) (SCH No. 201532006) that was 
prepared for the Clean Water Program. The Final PEIR was certified by City Council on June 6, 2016. The City prepared 
addenda to the Final PEIR that was approved on July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is 
within the scope of the Project evaluated in the PEIR and Addendum.

SUBJECT:
Wastewater Treatment Plant Annual Major Components Improvements — Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Award an agreement to C. Overaa & Co. for the Annual Major Components 3 Water Pumping Improvements and Ferric 
Chloride to Combined Sludge Line Project in an amount not to exceed $2,377,000; establish a contingency reserve in the 
amount of $475,400; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form 
presented and issue change orders as allowed by the contract documents and within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Clean Water Program (CWP) Annual Major Components (AMC) Projects includes several capital improvement projects 
that are currently under development or under construction and are intended to upgrade or rehabilitate aging 
infrastructure in the City’s sewer collection system and Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP). The 3 Water Pumping 
Improvements and Ferric Chloride to Combined Sludge Line project was identified as one of these projects. 
The project comprises of three major components. The first includes replacement of the four existing 3 Water pumps and 
ancillary systems (”3 Water” refers to disinfected effluent suitable for reuse throughout the WWTP). The 3 Water pumps 
system provides reclaimed flush water to the centrifuges, foam removal at the gravity thickeners, and hose bibs around 
the plant. The existing 3 Water pumps are nearing the end of their useful lives. The pump pedestals are corroded, and the 
piping is degraded. The project includes replacement of 3 Water pumps, associated piping, demolition of existing piping 
and appurtenances, and installation of a new valve on a 14-inch reclaimed water line. 
The second component includes replacement of the existing 10,000-gallon ferric chloride tank with a smaller day tank. 
Field investigations revealed that the slab under the existing ferric chloride tank is under stress and would require a load 
under 6,000 gallons to avoid retrofit work. The day tank would be supplied from the new ferric chloride chemical storage 
tanks constructed as part of the WWTP Upgrade and Expansion (GMP-3) Project. This would also reduce the chemical truck 
loading locations from two locations to one location at the new chemical storage tank area. The project includes the ferric 
chloride day tank, new ferric chloride metering pumps, a ferric chloride transfer pump, connections to ferric chloride yard 
piping and associated appurtenances, and demolition of existing piping and appurtenances. 
The third major component of the project includes replacement of four existing spent backwash pumps to four 
stormwater pumps to drain the detention basins that are used to retain storm water at the WWTP. The backwash pumps 
were originally used to convey spent backwash from the filter vessels. The filter vessels are not in service and have been 
abandoned and removed. The project includes construction of stormwater pump improvements in the Pump Pit, including 
demolition of existing spent backwash pumps, installation of new stormwater pumps and associated discharge and suction 
header. Potholing is included to locate existing utilities and stormwater connections, including excavation, backfill, 
compaction, pavement restoration, demolition of existing yard piping and connections to existing piping, as needed.
336 of 349

--- page 337 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Bid Results 
The Engineer’s Estimate for the Project is $4,820,000. The Project was advertised on October 2, 2025, and a total of six (6) 
bids were received and opened on November 6, 2025. The bids received are listed below in order of increasing bid 
amounts. While the bids received were lower than the Engineers Estimate, it should be noted that the Engineers Estimate 
was a conservative estimate based on previous bids that were influenced by supply changes issues and higher material 
costs as a result of COVID. The bids we received on this project may be an indication that the impacts to the supply chain 
of material are being resolved.  Staff reviewed the bids and determined that C. Overaa & Co. is the lowest responsive and 
responsible bidder, with a bid of $2,377,000 (comparison to Engineer’s Estimate in Attachment 2). Therefore, staff 
recommends for Council to award the construction agreement to C. Overaa & Co. Staff also recommends a $475,400 
contingency be established to address unknown challenges due to the complexity of sequencing and minimizing impact to 
operations when replacing existing infrastructure, underground and electrical tie-ins, and coordination with concurrent 
projects.

submitted to mediation. The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request. The 
mediator shall be agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties 
shall each submit one name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, 
the California State Board of Mediation and Conciliation, or other agreed-upon service. The 
mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties. Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party. No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement. The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

Exhibit A 
Insurance Requirements for Construction Contracts
Contractor shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract, and for x years thereafter, 
insurance against claims for injuries to persons or damages to property which may arise from or in 
connection with the performance of the work hereunder by the Contractor, his agents, 
representatives, employees, or subcontractors. 
MINIMUM SCOPE AND LIMIT OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 covering CGL 
on an “occurrence” basis, including products and completed operations, property damage, bodily 
injury and personal & advertising injury with limits no less than $5,000,000 per occurrence. If a 
general aggregate limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this 
project/location (ISO CG 25 03 or 25 04) or the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required 
occurrence limit.  
2. Automobile Liability:  Insurance Services Office Form CA 0001 covering Code 1 (any auto), with 
limits no less than $5,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation insurance as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, 
and Employers’ Liability insurance with a limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Builder’s Risk (Course of Construction) insurance utilizing an “All Risk” (Special Perils) coverage 
form, with limits equal to the completed value of the project and no coinsurance penalty 
provisions.
5. Surety Bonds as described below.
6. Professional Liability (if Design/Build), with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence or 
claim, and $2,000,000 policy aggregate.
7. Contractors’ Pollution Legal Liability and/or Asbestos Legal Liability and/or Errors and Omissions 
(if project involves environmental hazards) with limits no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or 
claim, and $2,000,000 policy aggregate.
If the contractor maintains broader coverage and/or higher limits than the minimums shown above, 
the Entity requires and shall be entitled to the broader coverage and/or higher limits maintained by 
the contractor. Any available insurance proceeds in excess of the specified minimum limits of insurance 
and coverage shall be available to the Entity.
Self-Insured Retentions 
Self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the Entity. At the option of the Entity, 
either: the contractor shall cause the insurer shall to reduce or eliminate such self-insured retentions 
as respects the Entity, its officers, officials, employees, and volunteers; or the Contractor shall provide 
a financial guarantee satisfactory to the Entity guaranteeing payment of losses and related 
investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses. The policy language shall provide, or be 
endorsed to provide, that the self-insured retention may be satisfied by either the named insured or 
Entity.
Other Insurance Provisions 
346 of 349

--- page 347 ---
Construction Contract
Page 8 of 9
Rev 1/24
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
1. The Entity, its officers, officials, employees, and volunteers are to be covered as additional 
insureds on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations performed 
by or on behalf of the Contractor including materials, parts, or equipment furnished in connection 
with such work or operations and automobiles owned, leased, hired, or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the Contractor. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an endorsement to 
the Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, CG 11 85 or both CG 20 10, 
CG 20 26, CG 20 33, or CG 20 38; and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
2. For any claims related to this project, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance coverage at least as broad as ISO CG 20 01 04 13 as respects the Entity, its officers, 
officials, employees, and volunteers. Any insurance or self-insurance maintained by the Entity, 
its officers, officials, employees, or volunteers shall be excess of the Contractor’s insurance and 
shall not contribute with it. 
3. Each insurance policy required by this clause shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, 
except with notice to the Entity.
Builder’s Risk (Course of Construction) Insurance 
Contractor may submit evidence of Builder’s Risk insurance in the form of Course of Construction 
coverage. Such coverage shall name the Entity as a loss payee as their interest may appear.
If the project does not involve new or major reconstruction, at the option of the Entity, an Installation 
Floater may be acceptable. For such projects, a Property Installation Floater shall be obtained that 
provides for the improvement, remodel, modification, alteration, conversion or adjustment to existing 
buildings, structures, processes, machinery and equipment.  The Property Installation Floater shall 
provide property damage coverage for any building, structure, machinery or equipment damaged, 
impaired, broken, or destroyed during the performance of the Work, including during transit, 
installation, and testing at the Entity’s site.
Claims Made Policies – (If at all possible avoid and require occurrence type CGL policies)
If any coverage required is written on a claims-made coverage form: 
1. The retroactive date must be shown, and this date must be before the execution date of the 
contract or the beginning of contract work.
2. Insurance must be maintained and evidence of insurance must be provided for at least five (5) 
years after completion of contract work. 
3. If coverage is canceled or non-renewed, and not replaced with another claims-made policy form 
with a retroactive date prior to the contract effective, or start of work date, the Contractor must 
purchase extended reporting period coverage for a minimum of five (5) years after completion 
of contract work. 
4. A copy of the claims reporting requirements must be submitted to the Entity for review. 
5. If the services involve lead-based paint or asbestos identification/remediation, the Contractors 
Pollution Liability policy shall not contain lead-based paint or asbestos exclusions. If the services 
involve mold identification/remediation, the Contractors Pollution Liability policy shall not 
contain a mold exclusion, and the definition of Pollution shall include microbial matter, including 
mold. 
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers authorized to conduct business in the state with a current A.M. 
Best rating of no less than A: VII, unless otherwise acceptable to the Entity. 
Waiver of Subrogation 
Contractor hereby agrees to waive rights of subrogation which any insurer of Contractor may acquire

from Contractor by virtue of the payment of any loss. Contractor agrees to obtain any endorsement

Verification of Coverage 
Contractor shall furnish the Entity with original Certificates of Insurance including all required

Subcontractors

Surety Bonds 
Contractor shall provide the following Surety Bonds:
1. Bid bond
2. Performance bond
3. Payment bond
4. Maintenance bond
The Payment Bond and the Performance Bond shall be in a sum equal to the contract price. If the 
Performance Bond provides for a one-year warranty a separate Maintenance Bond is not necessary.  If 
the warranty period specified in the contract is for longer than one year a Maintenance Bond equal to 
10% of the contract price is required.  Bonds shall be duly executed by a responsible corporate surety, 
authorized to issue such bonds in the State of California and secured through an authorized agent with 
an office in California.
Special Risks or Circumstances
Entity reserves the right to modify these requirements, including limits, based on the nature of the risk, 
prior experience, insurer, coverage, or other circumstances.
